Commander-in-Chief Chiang's Arrival in Hankou 68

Hankou Communication on the 21st: Commander-in-Chief Chiang arrived in Jiangxi from Nanjing at the beginning of this month to supervise the suppression of bandits and communists. He then took the opportunity to visit Lushan and summoned important generals from Hunan and Hubei provinces to meet him in Lushan. The local headquarters and the headquarters of the Third Army received a telegram from Commander-in-Chief on the 20th, stating that he would arrive in Hankou by ship on that day and instructing not to alarm various agencies and organizations. Therefore, the headquarters followed the order and did not notify various parties, but the provincial government urgently telegraphed the public security bureaus of various ports along the river to report the time of the Yong Sui warship's passage through the port in order to arrange security and gather to welcome him. At 2:00 AM that night, the Chu Qian warship docked at the Han River received a wireless telegraph from the Chu You and Yong Sui warships, stating that they had anchored near Huangzhou. It was estimated that they would arrive in Hankou at 12:00 noon on the 21st. After hearing the news, all circles here dispatched representatives to the Sanbei Company wharf one after another at 9:00 AM on the 21st to welcome him. The security forces were commanded by Liu Hantao, the commander of the 77th Regiment of the 13th Division. The first security line was responsible by the security department's mobile brigade. The second security line was responsible by the 77th Regiment of the 13th Division. The headquarters' guard brigade was responsible for guarding the inner streets and the vicinity of the Diplomatic Commissioner's Office. Sentries were stationed along the way by the 283rd Regiment of the 48th Division and the Gendarmerie Battalion. The Water Police Bureau patrolled the river surface, and personnel from the Inspection Office and the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau maintained order on the scene. Although the north wind was biting and it was raining and snowing, the order was still very strict. As for the welcoming personnel, there were hundreds of military officers above the rank of major general and civilian officials above the selected rank. On the military officer side, there were General Commander He Chengjun, Xia Douyin, Xu Yuanquan, He Jian, Division Commander Zhao Guantao, Fan Mingsheng, Xiao Zhichu, Fan Xiji, Xie Bin, Yuan Ying, Hao Mengling, Yue Weijun, Guo Runian, Deputy Division Commander Luo Zhuoying, Brigade Commander Wan Yaohuang, Wang Naiwen, etc., and Headquarters Chief of Staff Xian Chuanjing, Third Army Headquarters Chief of Staff Chen Guangzu, Security Department Chief of Staff Ye Peng, and Zhao Dajun, Director of the Managerial Office in Desert, etc. On the civilian officer side, there were Fang Benren, Wu Xingya, Liu Wendao, Xiong Bingkun, Huang Jianzhong, Hua Jueming, Chen Keming, Li Boren, and Provincial and Municipal Party Committee Liu Baifang, Yang Zaichun, Zuo Duo, Wang Shi[blank], Wen Juntian, Yu Yuzhi, and Qiu Hongjun, etc. The security department separately issued three types of red special symbols, yellow ordinary symbols, and boarding passes in advance. The scene was quite grand for a time. Until 1:10 PM, the Yong Sui warship approached from afar. All Chinese and foreign warships anchored in the Han River raised flags and fired twenty-one salute guns to pay their respects. The sound of gunfire rumbled and shook the entire city. The Yong Sui warship also fired salute guns in response. After the warship docked, Director He led the personnel above the rank of division commander and Fang Benren, Wu Xingya, Liu Wendao, etc. to board the ship to pay their respects for about ten minutes. At this time, the weather suddenly cleared, and the rain and snow stopped slightly. At 1:30 PM, Commander-in-Chief Chiang slowly disembarked wearing a gray military uniform and a black coat, looking energetic. Those who disembarked with him included Central Committee member Wu Weihui, Shao Lizi, Director of the Political Training Department Zhou Fohai, and welcoming personnel. At that time, the military and police raised their guns, and the military band played music in unison. Civilian and military officials also took off their hats and stood in respect. Commander-in-Chief Chiang raised his hand, smiled, and returned the salute. Mr. Wu Zhihui wore a gray patriotic cloth robe and an old top hat, walked with a calm pace, and looked extremely vigorous. After arriving ashore, Commander-in-Chief Chiang and Mr. Wu took car number 626 directly to the Diplomatic Commissioner's Office. Director He and the division commanders followed in cars. After Chiang arrived at the headquarters, he briefly inquired about the situation from the generals and then rested. This reporter went to the headquarters to meet Central Committee member Shao Lizi. According to him, Commander-in-Chief Chiang set off from Lushan at 8:00 AM on the 20th and departed from Jiujiang at 11:00 AM, accompanied by Mr. Wu Zhihui, Director Zhou Fohai, and himself (Shao self-proclaimed). In addition, there were Chief of Staff of the Headquarters Lin Wei and dozens of staff members, as well as a battalion of the guard brigade. The Minquan and Chu You warships also followed from Xunyang to escort him to Hankou. The number of days Commander-in-Chief will stay in Hankou and the date of return to Nanjing are currently undetermined. This reporter then visited Director Zhou Fohai. According to him, Commander-in-Chief Chiang's trip to Hunan may be canceled, and the trip to Xi'an is even more uncertain. The number of troops suppressing bandits in Jiangxi Province has increased and are actively suppressing bandits according to plan. Deng Ying was dismissed and severely punished for his ineffectiveness in suppressing bandits and is currently under guard by the Jiangxi Provincial Government. In addition to the first batch of Headquarters staff led by Adjutant General Zhan Zhenhuang who have arrived in Hankou, there were more than forty people who arrived with him that day.

Hankou Communication on the 22nd: After Commander-in-Chief Chiang arrived in Hankou on the 21st, he summoned He Chengjun, He Jian, Xia Douyin, Xu Yuan, Xiao Zhi, Fan Shisheng, Fan Xiji, Yue Weijun, Guo Ru, Yuan Ying, Fang Benren, Wu Xingya, Liu Wendao, etc. to inquire about the situation of bandit suppression. He Jian also requested to meet Chiang again at 4:00 PM on the 21st. Commander-in-Chief Chiang gave detailed instructions on the Hunan Province bandit suppression plan. He then returned to Hunan by car with his entourage at 8:00 PM that night. On the 22nd, Commander-in-Chief Chiang met with representatives and generals. He also hosted a banquet for military officers at 7:00 PM, which was very busy. The situation is recorded as follows:

Meeting with He Jian: Commander-in-Chief Chiang met with He Jian, Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government and Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Route Army, at 4:00 PM on the 21st. He gave a very detailed report on the recent situation of the communist bandits in Hunan Province and the progress of the suppression. Commander-in-Chief Chiang then ordered He to return to Hunan as soon as possible to preside over everything. He returned to Hunan by express train with his entourage at 8:00 PM, leaving Song Hegeng, Gao Daoshun, and Wang Dazhen of the Provincial Committee in Hankou to inquire whether Commander-in-Chief Chiang would go to Hunan. However, the Hunanese in Hankou believed that Commander-in-Chief Chiang would reward and punish those who suppressed bandits. Deng Ying had already been dismissed and severely punished for losing Ji'an, so it was not appropriate to be lenient to those responsible for losing Changsha. They specially formed a petition group to rescue Hunan and petitioned the Commander-in-Chief. However, Chiang was too busy and did not meet them today, according to reports.

Meeting with Representatives: Commander-in-Chief Chiang instructed the headquarters to schedule meetings with representatives from various places and military officers above the rank of army commander, division commander, brigade commander, and regimental commander. The headquarters immediately issued an urgent notice stating that Commander-in-Chief Chiang instructed to meet with representatives from various places at 10:00 AM on the 22nd and to instruct military officers above the rank of army commander, division commander, brigade commander, and regimental commander at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. Unless otherwise notified, it is hoped that they will go to Commander-in-Chief's office at the specified time and wait for the summons. By 7:00 AM on the 22nd, the representatives had arrived at the headquarters. Commander-in-Chief Chiang summoned them by name, including Li Zhigang, representative of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, and Zhang Buxian, representative of the Guizhou Provincial Government. He then met with former Acting Chairman of Hubei Province Fang Benren, Wang Cibo, representative of the 22nd Route Army stationed in Nanjing, Zhang Yinxiang, commander of the 30th Division, Peng Jinzhi, commander of the Third Brigade of the First Division, Peng Qibiao, deputy commander of the Fourth Division, Hu Yuza, director of the Hanyang Arsenal, Zhou Xingtang, Huang Wenzhi, and other representatives of the Hankou General Chamber of Commerce.

Summoning Generals: At 1:00 PM, Commander-in-Chief Chiang summoned military officers above the rank of army commander to inquire about their hometowns, ages, backgrounds, experiences, and the recent situation of their troops. After the generals reported, Chiang made pertinent criticisms and earnestly instructed them to improve military discipline and protect the people as the permanent struggle of the party and the country, and awarded each regimental commander 300 yuan as encouragement. From 1:00 PM to 7:00 PM, they were summoned in batches and comforted one by one. However, Han Jie, commander of the temporarily compiled Independent Second Brigade, was said to have been detained.

Banquet and Meeting: After Commander-in-Chief Chiang met with the representatives and generals, he hosted a banquet for the generals at the Diplomatic Commissioner's Office that evening, including General Commander of the First Army He Chengjun, General Commander of the Sixteenth Route Army Xu Yuanquan, General Commander of the Twenty-first Route Army Xia Douyin, Commander of the Sixth Division Zhao Guantao, Commander of the Fifty-fourth Division Hao Mengling, Commander of the Forty-fourth Division Xiao Zhichu, Commander of the Seventy-sixth Division Li Wanlin, Commander of the Fifty-first Division Fan Shisheng, Commander of the Twenty-sixth Division Guo Runian, Commander of the Thirty-fourth Division Yue Weijun, Commander of the Seventieth Division Fan Longgeng, Commander of the Sixty-eighth Division Li Wanru, Commander of the Sixty-ninth Division Liang Guanying, and Wu Xingya, Director of the Hubei Department of Civil Affairs, Liu Wendao, Mayor of Hankou, and dozens of others. During the banquet, Commander-in-Chief Chiang gave extremely important instructions and decided to convene a military conference with the commanders-in-chief, army commanders, division commanders, Wu Xingya, and Liu Wendao after the banquet to instruct on bandit suppression and politics.

Inspection of Troops: At 8:00 AM on the 23rd, he went to the new barracks in Qiaokou to inspect the troops of the Wuhan North District Fortress Command and gave instructions. On the 24th, he went to the Wuhan Military Academy to inspect and give instructions, which had been arranged by Yin Zusheng, Commander of the Wuhan North District Fortress, and Xue Lian, Chief of Staff of the Third Training Division, respectively. The welcome rally of all circles will be held after instructions are requested. Wu Jingheng, Shao Lizi, and Zhou Fohai, members of the Central Committee, who came to Hankou with Chiang, had their lectures scheduled by He Chengjun at the Provincial Government at 3:00 PM on the 23rd, and all subordinate agency staff have been notified to gather at the Provincial Government Auditorium to listen to the lectures.

Chiang's Itinerary: Chiang's original schedule after departing from Nanjing was to first visit Jiangxi, then Hubei, and then Hunan. However, after He Jian was summoned to Lushan, all the bandit conditions in Hunan Province were reported in detail. After Chiang arrived in Hankou, He asked for instructions and then returned to Hunan. It seems that Chiang does not need to go to Hunan. Moreover, the New Year's Day military parade in Nanjing is not far away, and it is difficult to go to Hunan from afar. However, according to today's news, Chiang will still go to Hunan after inspecting the Wuhan Military Academy on the 24th, either by warship, special train, or plane. It is not yet determined. According to another source, he will go to Xinyang and then return to Hankou and then to Nanjing. As for the trip to Hunan Province, He Chengjun will be sent as a representative. It is not yet certain which statement is correct.

Gong Bingfan's Division Captures Donggu 69

Donggu and Jinggang are Equally Famous

It is an Important Nest of the Communist Party

Rescued 300 Hostages

Killed Over 1,000 Bandits

Luo Lin Captures Yifu on the Same Day

Nanchang Communication: Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang's troops gathered in the southeastern part of Jiangxi Province in Le'an, Ningdu, Xingguo, and the southwestern part in Suichuan, Wan'an, Taihe, Anfu, and Lianhua. The 6th, 9th, and 19th Route Armies were divided into routes to encircle and suppress them. The 9th Route Army advanced southeast along the Gan River. The 19th Route Army recovered Yongxin, Lianhua, Taihe, and Suichuan from Pingxiang, bypassed the Gan River, and detoured south of Xingyu to prevent the communist bandits from fleeing to Guangdong. The 6th Route Army attacked forward from eastern Jiangxi towards Zhao Xie of Le'an and Qia Village of Nanfeng, bypassing Ruijin and Shicheng to reach Ningdu and cut off Zhu and Mao from entering Fujian. After the deployment was completed, the entire army launched a general offensive on the 16th. Because Donggu was the base camp of Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang, and the terrain was dangerous, and all kinds of agencies were available, it was no less than the second Jinggang. Special attention was paid to attacking Donggu. Gong Bingfan's division attacked the front of Donggu, Luo Lin's division took the right wing to capture Anfu and connect with the 19th Route Army. Tan Daoyuan and Xu Kexiang's two divisions took the left wing to connect with the 6th Route Army. Starting from the 16th, the central route went straight to Xingyu, closely pressing the left and right to take the encirclement. Luo's division captured Gujiang and occupied Anfu on the 17th. Gong and Zhang's two divisions also broke the line of the communist bandits in Futian, Shuikou, and Baisha on the 17th, and advanced bravely. On the 18th, Gong's division defeated the communist bandit Liu Tiechao's troops and directly approached Donggu. However, the communist bandits built strong fortifications there and defended the dangerous terrain. On the morning of the 19th, Gong's division's soldiers charged the communist bandits more than ten times, engaging in fierce hand-to-hand combat. Gong Bingfan also personally led the Chai brigade to advance, and there were also airplanes to assist in the battle. Until noon, Donggu Mountain was completely occupied, 300 hostages were rescued, more than 1,000 bandits were killed, and countless weapons and supplies were seized, and many machines were recovered. The communist bandits collapsed and retreated to the Ningyu area. At this moment, the 6th Route Army arrived in Guangchang and Ningdu, the 19th Route Army copied to Xingguo, and the 9th Route Army also advanced to the northwest of Xingning. Therefore, the communist bandits were already in a four-sided encirclement. Yesterday, the victorious telegrams from Gong's division and Zhang's division reported the victory. The original telegrams are as follows:

The New Fifth Division's victory telegram briefly stated: (After our division recovered Futian, Mao Zedong's bandit troops collapsed to the right wing of the mountains. Division Commander Gong then sent Wang Maode, commander of the Ninth Brigade, to supervise his troops to pursue Donggu directly. On the 18th, they met Liu Tiechao's troops again halfway and fought fiercely twice, killing the pseudo-regimental commander Gao Kecheng, the pseudo-battalion commander Guo Guohua, and more than 300 bandits, and seized more than 30 long and short guns and countless weapons. On the morning of the 19th, Brigade Commander Wang ordered the 18th Regiment to advance towards Donggu via Baishicheng Gangxu, and led the 19th Regiment to take the Ninety Ridge and advance separately with the 18th Regiment. Division Commander Gong also personally led the Chai brigade and the replenishment regiment to assist from behind. Officers and soldiers of each unit fought fiercely and broke the enemy's strong trenches and finally broke Donggu at noon on the 19th. Zhu Peng's remaining bandits collapsed towards Gulonggang. More than 1,000 bandits were killed in this battle and three mortars and more than 270 long and short guns and countless weapons and flags were seized. Our division also suffered more than 200 casualties. Donggu has a dangerous terrain and has always been the base of the communist bandits in Jiangxi. Among them, there are communist bandits' schools, hospitals, and various levels of Soviet governments, and the electric lights and sewing machines that were previously in Ji'an were also transported to Donggu for the purpose of defending to the death. After our army recovered Donggu this time, it has taken back the electric lights and sewing machines and rescued more than 200 male and female hostages. With the bandit nest broken, the bandit forces are shaken, and the elimination of the remnants is just around the corner.)

The 18th Division's victory telegram briefly stated: A subordinate unit recovered Shuinan this afternoon. The people along the way escaped completely, the fields were barren, and corpses were lying everywhere. Reddish textbooks of the school, Donggu Agricultural and Industrial Bank paper money, and slogans of overthrowing counter-revolutionaries, avoiding war, and opportunists Mao Zedong were searched. According to the coerced people, Mao indeed had anti-Zhu actions, etc., which shows that the internal division of the communist bandits is not difficult to suppress. This is hereby telegraphed to the Party Department of the 108th Regiment. Principles for Drafting the Farmers' Association Law 70

Already Determined by the Central Political Conference

The principles for the legislation of the Farmers' Association Law have been revised and passed by the 253rd meeting of the Central Political Conference on the 10th of this month and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for drafting. Now, the Legislative Yuan has resolved at the 122nd meeting to instruct the Farmers' Association Law Drafting Committee to take note. The principles are recorded as follows:

Principles of the Farmers' Association Law: (1) The Farmers' Association aims to develop the farmers' economy, increase the farmers' [blank], improve the farmers' lives, and promote agricultural development and improvement. (2) The Farmers' Association should handle the following matters: 1. Land and water conservancy improvement matters; 2. Seed, fertilizer, and agricultural tool improvement matters; 3. Forest cultivation and protection matters; 4. Disaster relief and prevention matters for floods and droughts; 5. Agricultural and farmer investigation and statistics matters; 6. Agricultural research and discussion matters; 7. Promotion and popularization of agricultural education and rural education matters; 8. Establishment of agricultural experiment fields matters; 9. Establishment of agricultural product display halls, agricultural [blank] display halls, and farmers' public libraries and reading rooms matters; 10. Holding farmers' public entertainment matters; 11. Promotion and guidance of cooperative undertakings such as production, consumption, credit, and warehouse matters; 12. Matters concerning the establishment of treatment centers, nurseries, and other old-age and poverty relief; 13. Grain storage and regulation matters; 14. Consulting and entrusting matters to the government; 15. Suggesting matters to the government for agricultural improvement and development; 16. Encouraging wasteland reclamation matters; 17. Other matters concerning agricultural development, improvement, guidance, publicity, and encouragement. (3) The Farmers' Association is a legal person. (4) Farmers' associations are divided into township farmers' associations, district farmers' associations, county and city farmers' associations, and provincial farmers' associations. (5) No more than two farmers' associations of the same level may be established in the same area. (6) Lower-level farmers' associations are members of higher-level farmers' associations. (7) Lower-level farmers' associations accept the entrustment of higher-level farmers' associations to carry out agricultural reporting and investigation matters. (8) Any person who resides in the township, is over 30 years old, and has one of the following qualifications may become a member of the township farmers' association: 1. Has farmland; 2. The area of cultivated farmland is 20 mu or more, or the area of cultivated garden land is 5 mu or more; 3. Graduates of secondary or higher schools who have studied agriculture; 4. Engages in businesses related to agriculture. (9) A township farmers' association is organized by 50 or more people who have the qualifications of members in the township and with the consent of one-third or more of those who have the qualifications of members in the township. (10) A provincial farmers' association, a county or city farmers' association, and a district farmers' association are each organized with the consent of more than half of their lower-level farmers' associations. (11) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce may convene a joint national farmers' association meeting when necessary. The aforementioned meeting may also be convened by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce if proposed by five or more provincial farmers' associations. (12) The committee system applies to provincial farmers' associations. Each county and the following farmers' associations shall have one secretary-general, one deputy secretary-general, and three to five secretaries. If necessary, with the approval of the competent authority in each locality, councilors may be appointed. (13) A farmers' association shall formulate its articles of association and submit them to the competent authority for record. (14) The supervisory authority of a provincial farmers' association is the provincial government where it is located. The supervisory authority of a county or city farmers' association, a district farmers' association, and a township farmers' association is the county or city government where it is located. (15) The areas of provincial farmers' associations, county or city farmers' associations, district farmers' associations, and township farmers' associations are based on the existing areas of provinces, counties, cities, districts, and townships. However, in special circumstances, the areas of district farmers' associations and township farmers' associations may not be based on the existing areas. (16) A farmers' association may not engage in profit-making businesses except for cooperative undertakings under Article 2, Item 11 with the permission of the competent authority.

League of Nations Health Director Visits China 71

Mr. Rajchman Passes Through Harbin Southward

Harbin Dispatch: Mr. Rajchman, the Health Director of the League of Nations Administrative Council, along with Mr. Wu Xiufeng, Secretary of the League of Nations Administrative Council Secretariat, and Mr. Jin Baoshan, Director of the National Government's Health Department, etc., passed through Harbin southward from Geneva on the 17th of this month. They are scheduled to stay in Peiping for several days before proceeding to Gaolaishi. According to Mr. Wu Xiufeng, their journey was approximately as follows: (They departed from Geneva, Switzerland, on December 5th, arrived in Warsaw on the 6th, departed from Warsaw on the 8th, and arrived in Moscow on the 9th. They changed trains on the same day and arrived at the border on the 17th.) Mr. Rajchman was invited by the National Government at the end of November this year to assist with China's health administration affairs. Mr. Rajchman also serves as a health advisor to the National Government. His actions will be dictated by the National Government. Last year, Mr. Rajchman came to China to negotiate a cooperation plan between the National Government and the League of Nations Health Organization. This plan has been approved by the National Government's Executive Yuan and the League of Nations, etc. Mr. Wu also said, "This year, the League of Nations re-elected its council members, and our country failed because: (1) Of the nine non-permanent council seats, one-third are re-elected each year. The Asian seat is currently held by Siam, and European and American countries are unwilling to have another Asian seat. (2) All countries have a negative impression of China due to the frequent civil wars in recent years. (3) Some countries have always opposed the system of re-election. (4) Countries are using the excuse that China has not been out of the Council for a full three years. Recently, with China unified and joining the League of Nations, their thoughts and perspectives have changed, and their expectations for our country are deep and great. The League of Nations also intends to provide China with talent and economic support, so there is hope for election in next year's Council re-election," etc. (18th)

Small Steamer on Wuhu-Nanjing Route Robbed 72

Wuhu Dispatch: The Yangtze River steamer directly from Wuhu to other ports, as well as inland river routes to Nanjing, Anqing, Datong, Nanling, Xuancheng, Wuwei, Hefei, Chaoxian, etc., have all been robbed by bandits in recent years. Except for the Nanjing route, none have escaped, and some have been robbed multiple times. Unexpectedly, the Nanjing route was also robbed today. The Da'an Company's new Ningxing steamer departed from Nanjing this morning (22nd) at 7:00 AM, carrying passengers upstream to Wuhu. At 11:30 AM, while sailing on the Yangtze River at the Sh牌 River, upstream of Wujiang, six men in short clothing, speaking with a Guangxi accent, who had boarded the ship in Nanjing, suddenly claimed to be inspectors. Three of them drew pistols from their sleeves, one drew a Mauser pistol, one drew a small knife, and one drew two hand grenades. They first inspected the two soldiers traveling on the ship, fearing that they were carrying weapons and would resist. The two soldiers said, "We are not carrying guns. How dare you impersonate inspectors..." Before they could finish speaking, the bandits opened fire on the two soldiers, hitting their heads and abdomens. At the same time, the man with the hand grenades went to the cabin, threatening to stop the ship. They immediately began searching the passengers and the ship's accounting office, stealing all cash and jewelry. This lasted for more than twenty minutes. They then forced the ship to sail to the vicinity of Heshan Port on the south bank of the Yangtze River, where they went ashore with their loot and fled. The ship arrived in Wuhu at 7:00 PM. Upon receiving the report, the military and police agencies sent personnel to board the ship for investigation. The two wounded soldiers died en route due to their serious injuries. One was Zhu Xingyou, a squad leader from the 341st Regiment of the 171st Brigade of the 57th Division stationed in Wuhu, who was going to Nanjing to pick up his family. His wife was crying bitterly on the ship. The other's letters showed that he was a soldier named Li from the 2nd Teaching Division stationed in Jiaxing. It is reported that the passengers' losses totaled about 2,000 yuan. (22nd)

Wuxi 76

Proposals for the Railway Bureau's business conference. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau is scheduled to convene a business conference from January 5th to 9th, soliciting opinions from chambers of commerce in various counties and relevant industries in advance in order to gather ideas and broaden perspectives. The Wuxi Chamber of Commerce has nominated Cheng Jingtang and Tang Xinghai as representatives to attend. Yesterday, they also put forward five proposals: (1) Trains arriving at various stations must strictly adhere to the announced schedule to avoid delays and convenience passengers. (2) At prosperous stations along the line, such as Wujin and Wuxi for southbound trains, and Wuxi and Wujin for northbound trains, the number of third- and fourth-class carriages should be increased as appropriate, and attention should be paid to cleanliness and improvement. (3) Although passenger transport on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway has been busy in recent years, freight transport is far less than before. Some goods that used to be transported by rail are now transported by ship. This is because, although there are regulations for loading and unloading, workers along the line often collude with each other to demand exorbitant fees. If their demands are not met, they often damage the goods or even steal them at will. Merchants cannot claim compensation and are unwilling to suffer losses, so they resort to shipping. Therefore, more freight cars should be provided at prosperous stations along the line, and strict rules should be established. If railway workers deliberately damage goods or steal them due to unmet demands, and merchants report and verify the facts, strict penalties should be imposed to protect merchants and expand freight transport. (4) Traffic on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is becoming increasingly congested, and the original single track is far from sufficient. Recent delays are mostly caused by waiting for trains. A plan should be drawn up within a reasonable period of time to lay double tracks to avoid obstruction and facilitate transportation. (5) Please investigate the plan proposed by the former Municipal Preparatory Office to build the Wuxi-Wuqiao Railway, moving the freight station to Wuqiao to connect with the Be塘 market, which would be convenient for transportation by the Railway Bureau and development of the local area. The above five proposals were sent to the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau yesterday for discussion at the meeting.

A man commits suicide by hanging due to oppression from his wife. Yang Chunsheng, a resident of Shiguqiao, Tangtou Township, in the Sixth District, was over thirty years old and worked as a crew member on a barge at the Yukang Yarn Factory. He had been married to his wife, Yang Shen, for more than ten years and had two sons and two daughters. In recent years, Chunsheng's income was not enough to cover expenses, so his wife Shen often quarreled with him. The other day, Chunsheng asked his wife for 2,000 yuan, but she refused and scolded him harshly, slapping him several times. Chunsheng, feeling humiliated, became disillusioned with life. He immediately came to the city, pawned his cotton robe for six yuan, spent four yuan on a haircut and meal, and used the rest to buy a hemp rope. He then walked back to his hometown and hanged himself in an empty room above Huachang Lane. A village woman who went inside to fetch firewood noticed that he was already dead. She immediately ran to tell his wife, Yang Shen. After hearing the news, she went and carried her husband Chunsheng home and bought a coffin for a hasty burial.

Special Educational News

Zheng Wuchang's Creation of the Entire Number of Stroke Form Character Index (1) 84

Recently, no fewer than dozens of new character indexing methods have been invented, all striving for simplicity. Among the more comparable methods that are generally popular are: (1) Character indexing using numbers; (2) Character indexing using stroke order. Although Arabic numerals are also commonly used, one has to recognize the strokes of the character, and also use numbers to remember the count. Using this indirect method is inevitably cumbersome, and one must have studied arithmetic beyond four digits to be able to apply it easily. As for talking about stroke order, it feels even more difficult, because people who do not recognize characters simply do not know where to start writing the character. Even those who are slightly familiar with stroke order may have different habits, and the order of strokes cannot be consistent. Therefore, using numbers and talking about stroke order is still not thinking from the perspective of the character indexing user. Moreover, there are actually nine distinct types of strokes in analyzing Chinese characters: (dot), (horizontal), (vertical), (撇), (curve) (strokes that are curved belong to this category), (fold) (strokes that turn and form acute angles belong to this category), (鉤), (捺), (　). Recently, people who use stroke count to index characters often intentionally reduce or combine the number of strokes, or merge several single strokes into a complex stroke, which feels completely without standard, causing confusion. I believe that character indexing methods needed by primary school students and ordinary households should at least (not use numbers), (not consider stroke order), and can be started for indexing without thinking. Although I dare not confidently say that the creation of the entire number of stroke form character index is very perfect, it can be said to be an "easy to index without learning" character indexing method. Now, I will disclose the simple explanation of the entire number of stroke form character index as follows, hoping that comrades at home and abroad will provide strict guidance and criticism.

(A) Count the entire number of strokes of the character to be indexed. Every turn in the stroke is counted as one stroke. One stroke counts as one stroke. For example,

(B) is counted as four strokes for horizontal-fold-horizontal-hook. (阡) is counted as eight strokes for horizontal-fold-curve-hook-vertical-徽-horizontal-vertical.

(　) is counted as seven strokes for horizontal-vertical-horizontal-vertical-horizontal-curve-hook. (酉) is counted as nine strokes for horizontal-vertical-horizontal-vertical-撇-vertical-horizontal-horizontal. (退) is counted as thirteen strokes for horizontal-vertical-horizontal-horizontal-vertical-　-撇-dot-dot-horizontal-vertical-捺.

(Note) (1) Several people have advocated counting each turn in the stroke as one stroke, but no one has ever defined the nine types of strokes as the basic strokes of Chinese characters.

(2) When counting, just count one, two, three, four according to the turning of the strokes, without having to recite the types of strokes and the stroke order.

(3) I randomly took more than 300 characters from the Chinese Character Dictionary published by Zhonghua Book Company, and asked four or five seven- or eight-year-old children who had just started school to count them individually, and then double-checked them, and there were no mistakes.

(4) It takes no more than ten minutes to count the total number of strokes of a Chinese character.

Life at Wellesley College (3) 85

(Sent from the United States by Lu Erzhao, Songjiang)

(E) Most students take test scores as their lives. Foreign students like us come here to study, and of course, we take learning as the premise, which goes without saying. However, Japanese students study even harder, with the intention of sacrificing their lives for learning. They sleep at 2:00 AM every night and get up at 6:30 AM, and their test scores are indeed passing. However, they are not necessarily outstanding, mostly because their pronunciation is not accurate and there are occasional mistakes in listening to and recording lectures. I expect that this problem will be eliminated after a few months. Erzhao and three other Chinese students are all graduates of Shanghai schools, and there is no obstacle in terms of language. Except for physical education, the test scores of each subject are fortunately ranked in the top tier. Teachers and classmates all attach importance to them. The three of us secretly made an agreement, saying that studying abroad is for the sake of the country, and our test scores must not be weak, and we must not disgrace the country. This heart and this strength will never be stolen. However, the days ahead are long, and we must encourage each other. Among the American students, those who are agile and studious actually account for the majority. There are a very small number of students who like to be surprised by the outside world, and those with slightly weaker test scores are mostly crying and weeping, soaking their handkerchiefs with tears, the same as famous girls' schools in Shanghai. We can pass physical education, but swimming is like eating glutinous rice balls, and we get circled scores. The professor is initially lenient and forgives, which makes people feel ashamed, but there is really nothing we can do. The three of us will work hard to encourage ourselves and be persistent.

Attached is a glimpse of the American unemployment problem by a professor.

The unemployment problem is rampant in countries around the world. It is regarded as one of the most difficult problems in the political world. The United States naturally joins the world's hot spot and becomes chaotic. Erzhao read the American Labor Yearbook and saw that in 1927, the total number of non-agricultural workers in the United States was 32,695,000, and the number of unemployed was 2,055,000, accounting for 6.3%. Also, I saw in the newspaper that President Hoover asked the House Appropriations Committee to allocate US$150 million for unemployment relief funds. The current officials and people in the United States regard the unemployment problem as a task that needs to be solved urgently. Yesterday, taking advantage of a professor's break after class, I asked him about this problem. The professor told me that the United States is the country with the fastest progress in productivity and efficiency. Many labor-saving machines have been invented, and scientific management methods are complete. Whether it is manufacturing, transportation, agriculture, or mining, it is possible to reduce labor and produce more. People with special skills have unemployment problems. Also, he said that there are no tariff barriers between the states in the United States, the land and resources are abundant, the population is not large, the machines are precise and fast, and the products are abundant. Immigration is strictly prohibited, and workers are paid high wages. The general national standard of living is naturally increased. It is said that increased wages and general national progress and prosperity are all caused by our United States, and the sharp increase in the number of unemployed is also not a small disaster for the United States. It is currently urgent to find ways to provide relief, but it is not a fundamental solution. Erzhao urgently asked about the fundamental and long-term method. The professor sighed and said, "Let's postpone talking about other places and just talk about my family. The old woman who used to work for us had a weekly wage of gold. Now this woman has asked for a break from work for more than two weeks. The reason is that the monthly wage for maids is different, but the total is always no more than 40 or 50 yuan. The government gives unemployed workers at least two gold yuan per week. Most of the idle workers voluntarily become unemployed." Erzhao asked again, "What is a good method to solve this unsolvable problem?" Just as the evening bell rang, the professor excused himself and said, "Let's study next time." (Recorded in the dormitory of Wellesley College, November 10, 1926) (The End)

Important News

The Chinese Astronomical Society Holds its Annual Meeting 86

Re-elects Officers and Passes Seven Resolutions

The Chinese Astronomical Society held its 8th annual meeting at the Astronomical Research Institute in Gulou, this city, on the 22nd of this month. More than twenty members attended, including Tu Yingwei, Chief of the Qingdao Meteorological Observatory, Xu Renxian, Professor of National Zhejiang University, and members from this city. The meeting opened at 9:00 AM. All the members present jointly elected Yu Qingsong, Director of the Astronomical Research Institute, as the chairman. After the opening ceremony, the chairman delivered an opening speech, saying, "The annual meeting of the Meteorological Society yesterday encountered heavy snow. Today, our association's annual meeting also happens to be blessed with clear skies. This is all a coincidence. The main purpose of meteorology is to study changes in weather, and rain and snow are the subjects of investigation. The most important task of astronomy is to observe the seven luminaries. The Astronomical Research Institute has recently acquired a new solar spectrograph. The clear weather today is a good opportunity for everyone to view it. In recent years, the domestic astronomical enterprise can be said to have developed with shame. The establishment of astronomical observatories and the establishment of astronomy departments in universities are often heard. This is a celebration for our party," etc. Next, the general secretary, Gao Jun, reported on the association's affairs, saying that the association's greatest achievements this year were: first, in addition to the yearbook, a monthly journal was added, which has been published on schedule every month since January of this year; second, the Variable Star Observation Committee was moved to Guangzhou and established earlier this spring, and began observation with excellent results. The chairman of the association, Zhang Yunqing, sent a report, which the chair will read. Finally, he reported on the storage and interest situation of the scholarship fund. After the report, the accountant, Li Feng, reported on the income and expenditure situation of this year's funds. Next, there was an academic lecture. First, member Zhang Yuzhe lectured on the special features of the variable star observation camera recently delivered to the Astronomical Research Institute. Member Gao Jun lectured on the structure and characteristics of the Hale solar spectroscope. After the lectures, members took turns visiting the instrument room for experimental viewing. At 12:00 noon, a group photo was taken, and then a banquet was held at the Gulou Restaurant. In the afternoon, a business meeting was held. First, the officers were re-elected. The elected officers included President Gao Lu, Vice President Yu Qingsong, Councillors Zhang Yuzhe, Chen Zhan　, and Zhao Jinyi, and General Secretary Gao Jun. Next, the motions were discussed. A total of seven cases were resolved. After the meeting adjourned, the Astronomical Research Institute hosted a banquet at the World Hotel.

(Kuomintang News Agency) The Nine District Party Headquarters of this city issued a declaration regarding the Guanghua University incident:

The declaration states: Tracing back to the May Thirtieth Incident, people across the nation deeply resented the brutality and tyranny of the imperialists, and the fact that church schools acted as their accomplices. Hence, the establishment of Guanghua University was intended to accommodate patriotic and nationalistic young people who sacrificed themselves for the nation. It was also meant to directly or indirectly oppose church schools acting as accomplices and the brutal, tyrannical imperialists. Guanghua's past cannot but be described as glorious, and the support of society cannot but be described as enthusiastic and responsible. Administrative personnel of Guanghua School should support this glorious history, promote it, and comfort the hopes of the association and the painstaking efforts of the students who have traveled far to study, without allowing it to be prematurely cut short or fall by the wayside. Unexpectedly, since Liao Shicheng, an important lackey of the Nationalist faction, became the principal, he has been colluding with others, occupying key positions, and treating those who are not members of the Nationalist faction as snakes and scorpions, and labeling them as "feudal remnants." Anyone who opposes the government or mocks the authorities is treated with deference, and those who are disreputable are treated as fathers and family members. Luo Longji and others, who usually advocate human rights and oppose the party, were able to seize the opportunity to be selected, and Fan Zhaocong, Hu Zuyin, and others, who repeatedly violated discipline and acted as accomplices in causing trouble, were able to swagger and jump around for a while. Now, we dare to report the process to our fellow compatriots. The Fifth Branch of this district is located within Guanghua University. Party member Fan Zhaocong repeatedly violated discipline and was absent from branch party member meetings. Standing Committee member Yang Shuchun questioned and warned him in accordance with the discipline. This is Fan Zhaocong's own fault, and he should accept it without resistance or dispute. Unexpectedly, when the incident occurred, Fan Zhaocong dared to resist the sanctions of discipline and oppose the party. Hu Zuyin, who has always been against party doctrine, dared to come out and act as an accomplice in creating chaos. Liao Shicheng, who has always flaunted nationalism, once was a lackey of Sun Chuanfang of Dongren University and a supporter of the Five-Color Flag Alliance, insisted that Yang Shuchun was guilty of assault and insisted on expulsion in order to satisfy his selfish desire to exclude dissidents and remove comrades from our party. Declarations and notices of our party were arbitrarily confiscated, and non-factional students were arbitrarily suppressed. If there was any negotiation, it was called disrespect for teachers, roaring provocations, and sowing discord. Under today's blue sky and white sun flag, such absurd facts exist. In Guanghua, which has a glorious revolutionary history, there is such a stain. This is what our party comrades cannot tolerate, and it is also what society does not approve of. On the contrary, it brings shame to Guanghua and ridicule to the Johnnies. On the night of the tenth, Guanghua students Xing Daocheng, Hu Zuyin, and others distributed communist slogans and leaflets. After the efforts of party comrades Yang Shuchun, Xu Jiying, and others to investigate, they were caught on the spot with witnesses and irrefutable evidence. Even if Su Zhang had the gift of the gab, he could not wash away the irrefutable evidence. Free Talk

Words from Those Who Attain Buddhahood 96

Among the Chinese people, the most economically minded are the people of Jiangbei. If all Chinese people were like the people of Jiangbei, they would definitely overthrow the Japanese.

People only seek food, which is not easy, so they neglect the health benefits of air. They do not know that diet can harm health and that breathing can prolong life.

Lao Tzu said, "Subtle, subtle, it seems to exist." Zhuang Tzu said, "The breath of the perfected man comes from his heels." These two phrases are the most profound in the way of breathing and nourishing life.

Beauty has no standard at first, and there is nothing that can be measured or estimated. As the saying goes, "Beauty is in the eye of the beholder." It is true.

It is common to see wealthy people who love goods and are greedy, leading to the ruin of their families. You must know that after a hundred years of life, even if you are buried in a golden coffin, it is difficult to avoid the danger of exhumation. What is the point?

A maxim is a prediction, so a gentleman does not believe in predictions but believes in maxims.

Air is of the greatest importance to people. Wind and rain are the flow of air. Heat and cold are the changes in air pressure. Qi in reverse causes anger, qi in stagnation causes sorrow, qi in ascent causes panting, qi in stagnation causes sickness. People's joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness are all like shadows that follow the form of qi. Therefore, a gentleman must nourish qi.

A person's forehead lines are like the tree rings of a tree. Botanists look at the tree rings of a tree to determine the tree's age, so looking at the number of forehead lines of people is enough to estimate the length of their life.

Yang Xingfo said that Chinese scholars can be divided into three stages: the youth stage is called the patriot, the prime of life stage is called the celebrity, and the old age stage is called the layman. In fact, the youth must embrace the ambition of a layman and act as a patriot, and the old age must have the ambition of a patriot and act as a layman. It is not without benefit to the country, but celebrities, no matter what stage they are in, must never be allowed to do it.

Snippets of Jiangxi Bandit Disaster Huang Yingdai 97

Jiangxi Province has been plagued by communist bandits recently, and the people are unable to make a living. Therefore, when Chairman Chiang made his tour, he first went to the Jiujiang and Nanchang areas. Yesterday, a guest returned to Shanghai from Jiujiang. After meeting and talking, I was informed of the recent situation in Jiangxi amidst the banditry. I am eager to record a few points to enrich this discussion. The market situation is peaceful. Although there are many rumors in the Jiujiang and Nanchang areas recently, the market situation is still good, and it has indeed improved in the past few weeks. There are enough troops in the city, and the communist bandits dare not come to commit crimes. However, Ji'an, which is three or four hundred miles away from Nanchang, was occupied by bandits for fourteen days. They looted, burned, and did all kinds of evil. The number of deaths and injuries was as high as thousands. However, the number of houses burned down was limited, and the losses of the church were not significant.

The Bandit's Momentum is Rampant. According to news from Nanchang, when the communist bandits were at the height of their power, they launched a large-scale attack and occupied many cities. However, the losses of the people in the places they went were not significant, and the churches were not seen to be burned down. As for the Christian and Roman churches in Nanchang, they suffered a lot of damage, and there were many priests who were kidnapped. Later, several people escaped from the bandit's den and were able to be reborn, which was the greatest good fortune in the midst of misfortune.

Strict Defense. In recent days, the defenses inside Nanchang city have been quite strict. Iron wire fences and defensive objects have been set up on the thoroughfares. There are plenty of troops, and the police patrol day and night to ensure safety. Therefore, the British and American priests who went to other places to take refuge have returned to the city one after another. Jiujiang and Guling are also quite peaceful, and it is believed that there will be no accidents.

General Prices. As far as the prices in Nanchang are concerned, the price of rice has never been so low. Currently, it is only five to eight yuan per picul, which is about 130 catties. Most other goods have risen sharply, such as food, leather goods, clothing, fuel, etc., which are all higher than usual.

A Further Account of the Xiong Family, an Old Student of Chih Chih.

A few days ago, I read "Free Talk" by Mr. Yun Xun, which described an old student of Chih Chih with some inaccuracies. I studied at Chih Chih and was in the same grade and department as this old student, so I know more details. I would like to add some details. This old student's surname is Lu, his name is Hongkun, and he is from Henan (the name of the county has been forgotten). He is over fifty years old and his beard is nearly half a foot long. Those who do not know him suspect that he is a teacher. When a classmate asked him how old he was, he replied that he was forty. He studied in the first grade of the political science department of the Faculty of Law and Politics at Chih Chih. Last year, he was at the National University of the Republic of China in Beijing. This semester, he moved to Shanghai to Chih Chih to take refuge from the Northern Expedition of the Central Army. He is not good at sports and likes to play chess at Dongxinqiao. Because of his age, he was appointed as the class leader, and his classmates were happy to associate with him and elected him as a member of the class meeting preparation committee and a representative to the student union. (Que Chou)

Usually, there have been many price increases. The wages of workers, except for those with contracts or special circumstances, are higher than in the past.

General Transportation Situation. The business in Jiujiang is still very lively, and the transportation of railway passengers and luggage in Nanchang is particularly busy. However, the water level in the Yangtze River is shallow, which will make navigation inconvenient. Construction projects in Nanchang city are underway, roads are being widened, and streets are being rebuilt. The number of automobiles and rickshaws has also increased. Therefore, although it is currently in an unfortunate state, it can be asserted that it will develop in the future.

Travels in the Southern Seas 99

Burmese women's wisdom, discussion, and influence in society far exceed those of our country. Those in the markets are mostly literate and numerate, having received a considerable amount of education and refined appearance. Even the most well-educated women in our country cannot compare. Moreover, they are rich in experience in handling social affairs, composed and generous, absolutely unlike the shyness of Chinese women. Their men, already transformed by the custom of monasticism, are no longer as barbaric as men of other countries. Therefore, women more easily engage in activities and develop their talents. Could it be that the monastic system is also a useful tool for softening men and achieving a world of universal harmony? The English scholar Bertrand Russell said, "Why not use the three-year compulsory military service to open rivers and repair projects?" I say it would be better to use it to make Burmese men become monks; is that the way to achieve a world of universal harmony? Some say Burmese men have already been subdued, and there is hardly any case of men daring to rape women. Others say that is not entirely true. I dare not make a definitive judgment.

Burmese women are also quite willing to marry Chinese men because they suffer from running their own businesses and wish to rely on husbands to alleviate their direct labor. Those women with property are also willing, as a rule, to share part of their family property with their husbands. Therefore, the wealth of middle-class men often relies on the help of marrying Burmese wives. However, one must know that their marriage and divorce are extremely free; if they don't get along, they divorce without any hesitation. Also, if a man marries a woman, he often becomes a live-in son-in-law, having to bear the living expenses of the woman's entire family. This refers to those without property.

Burmese people of both sexes love singing and dancing. All customs of primitive peoples have this freedom, but as etiquette and doctrine arose, this custom gradually diminished. Now, the people of Guangxi are still close to this. The attitude of men and women displayed in the portraits seen on the streets is very different from that in other countries. Sometimes, men lie in women's arms as guests, while women act as masters. One can know their social customs.

The custom of Indian women is to wear gold and silver rings on their noses, ears, and feet. Burmese women are generally ignorant of all this, more or less the same as Chinese women. Those Chinese women dressed as Burmese cannot distinguish the authenticity. Also, Indian women have long faces and high noses, with a slightly dark complexion. Burmese women are white and delicate, due to different races and bloodlines.

Li Shizeng went to Ping from Tianjin to discuss matters with Cheng Yanqiu regarding the development of the Chinese Opera Music Academy. (Chaoran)

Warmth in the Heart (34) Bao Tianxiao 126

Chapter Sixteen: Cui Xiu Earnestly Asks for Words from the Teacher, and the Heroine Generously Discusses Military Affairs at a Brothel Banquet.

The next day, Zuo Shichen got up early and went to the Commercial Press to buy many elementary Chinese language textbooks. According to them, she had already read the first and second books, so this time they could start with the third book, as well as calligraphy templates, brushes, and paper, as well as "Children's World," "Children's Readings," etc., totaling a large bundle, just like sending a child to school. At this time, it was the beginning of the second month of the old lunar calendar, and the schools were also starting the spring semester. Male and female students were crowded in front of the counters of the two major bookstores, all matching their books. Zuo Shichen was also crowded among them. A receptionist in the bookstore recognized Zuo Shichen and came to greet him, saying, "Oh, Mr. Zuo, are you also here to buy books? Is Mr. Zuo teaching at that school now, or are these textbooks for the young lady and young master in your family?" Zuo Shichen's face turned red when he was asked, and he had to answer vaguely. The receptionist was very enthusiastic and quickly said to a clerk, "This is Mr. Zuo Shichen. Please match his books first to save Mr. Zuo from waiting for a long time." Zuo Shichen also said, "Please do, please do," but the receptionist went to greet other people. Zuo Shichen carried a large package of books to the small garden. It was only four or five o'clock in the afternoon, and Luyi's mother had not yet come out of her small mansion. Luyi was also wearing a casual suit of clothes with a light blue bamboo cloth vest over it. They called it a dressing-up jacket. Although her hair was already done, she had not yet removed the jacket. The sleeves of the jacket were turned out over a blue striped flannel short shirt. Seeing Zuo Shichen carrying a paper package, she said, "Have the books been bought?" She eagerly untied it and looked at it, just like a child. She was very happy to see the pictures in "Children's World" and other things. She looked at this one and then at that one, greatly enjoying the pleasure of a child getting a cake. Seeing a picture of someone playing a ball, she said, "I used to have a ball, and I could pat it more than a hundred times. Now that ball is broken." Zuo Shichen said, "That's easy. Next time I go to the Commercial Press, I'll give you a big ball." Seeing a picture of someone playing the harmonium and singing, she said, "I used to go to a girls' school for three months, and they also had a singing class. I still remember the singing teacher teaching us a song about letting go of the feet, singing something (bound feet are the most bitter, bitter from childhood to old age). However, those song collections did not distinguish between men and women. There was also something (a boy's first ambition is high, to make meritorious service in battle in the future). We were very reluctant to sing those many songs, saying that they were sung by male students, but the teacher said that there were also female revolutionaries singing during the revolution the year before. Soon there will be equal rights for men and women. Making meritorious service in battle cannot be left to men alone. Could it be that women will really be taught to fight in the future?"

Grain and Rice Market Declines Gradually 136

Zhabei: Yesterday, at over forty locations on Luli Road and the main street, sales remained slow. The route for North Japonica rice was slightly more active, but focused on high-quality goods, so the price of high Japonica rice gradually fell by about two jiao. The market remained sluggish. Top Grade Opened at 13 Yuan 6 Jiao. Subgrade only 12 Yuan. Thin Rice arrivals were slightly scarce, and sales were unpromising, recovering briefly by a jiao. Semi-early rice was slightly soft. Sheep Xian rice trended towards flat, but below average quality was reduced by one jiao. Market conditions: High prices were stable, subgrade was sluggish. Du Jian and Bu Jian buying interest was weak. Source gradually lowered prices by one jiao, turning cloudy. While arrivals were not many, guest sales and liquor demand were both weak, so prices remained soft. Top grade changed, opening at 13 Yuan 3 Jiao.

Shanghai South: Yesterday, over twenty boats arrived from downriver. Sales from all directions were sluggish. Changbang and Sutong brands of machine-milled Japonica rice continued to see downstream stores and stomachs taking a wait-and-see approach, because the end of the year was near, and importers were consolidating, leading to reduced transactions. The overall market fell by 1-2 jiao. The Nambang early rice situation was also slow; with sales remaining sluggish, sellers became more willing to sell, and prices gradually fell by half a jiao. Sheep Du Xian sales were unpromising. High-quality goods were rare, so the market was stable. Subgrade sales were weak, slightly down. Ordinary grades were turning cloudy with few patrons, and prices were down a small jiao. Throughout the day, both the North and South markets continued to be uniformly sluggish.

Flour and Wheat Market Fell Sharply, Then Recovered Slightly 137

Flour: Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, prices for all months again showed a sharp decline. The reported price for foreign wheat for distant futures in Chicago also fell by a small seven jiao, and Canadian near and far futures each fell by five jiao, with recent futures actually shrinking to just over five jiao, again hitting a record low. Therefore, after the price drop, people inside and outside the industry were very worried. (Rumor on the market was that factories were continuing to order three yuan worth of foreign wheat). The opening price immediately fell sharply. This month's price was lowest at 2.0925 taels. January's price was 2.065 taels, February's was 2.0525 taels, March's was 2.075 taels, April's was 2.08 taels, and May's was 2.09 taels, falling 1.1325 taels from the previous day's closing price for recent futures and falling 1.0 fen for distant futures. However, since the second round, due to outsiders short selling frantically, the market recovered. When the afternoon session opened, the market seemed slightly stable because short sellers were still covering, but in general, the decline was still difficult to reverse. As a result, this month's price was down a small 0.075 tael from the previous day. January to March was down a small 0.015 tael, and April and May were down a small 0.0125 tael.

Wheat: Yesterday, after the wheat futures market opened in the morning, prices for foreign wheat continued to fall by 0.5-0.7 jiao, causing people to become agitated again. The lowest price for January and February was 4.08 taels. March and April were 4.09 taels, and May was 4.11 taels. Because short sellers were still quiet, the market did not see a sharp change. When the afternoon session opened, the Shanghai-Ningbo and Shaoxing gangs had to close their positions due to the end of the year, and because they were eager to cover their short positions, the market improved slightly, increasing by 0.05-0.06 tael from the lowest price. As a result, January was unchanged, February was down a small 0.01 tael, March and April were unchanged, and May was down a small 0.01 tael. The spot wheat market was still sluggish. Only the opening price for 2,000 packages of wheat from Daoren Bridge was 3.06 taels, handled by Huafeng.

Sugar Market Opens with 2,000 Bags of Cuban Raw Sugar 138

Yesterday's sugar market: According to news from the production areas, Cuban spot sugar prices were unchanged. New York sugar futures for December rose by 0.06 yuan, and March of next year fell by 0.01 yuan. Other months were unchanged. Java spot and futures prices were also unchanged. The market was gradually enlivened by the high exchange rate outside the Public Association market. The buying interest for Dutch sugar #24 Coarse Sand White was slightly strong, with over a thousand bags traded at a price of 8.4 taels. The market was still stable. #20 Medium Sand White was 7.75 taels, with a shortage of sellers, quoting 7.8 taels. #8 Raw Red was 7.15 taels. Brand was 7.4 taels. The market was slightly up compared to the usual sugar market. Z Mark was 8.6 taels to 8.625 taels. YT Mark was 8.4 taels. YRO Mark was 7.9 taels. YP Mark was 8.875 taels to 8.9 taels. Meiji YP Mark was 8.925 taels. J Mark was 9.2 taels. The market was very brisk. The market for brand goods: The Chinese product Tongshou Bingyu Chun brand opened up, rising to 6.6 taels, but demand was very sparse, and the market was very sluggish. Huaxin opened for sale 2,000 bags of Cuban raw sugar at a price of 7.1 taels. These were purchased by local factories for use in refining ice flower and green raw materials.

North-South Goods, Wood Ear Mushroom Gradually Rises 10 Taels 139

The lowest price for wood ear mushroom in the previous market was 83-84 taels. Recently, with the conclusion period extended to January 15, sentiment suddenly turned upward. Goods from Malanping are now gradually rising to 93 taels, an increase of nearly two in relation to the lowest price. Dealers are selling at 95 taels, with a flourishing trend. Other miscellaneous goods are also rising with the trend, with tight supplies.

Oil Market, White Tung Oil Sales Clear, Prices Rise 140

This year, the cost of white tung oil in the production areas is high. Merchants in Hanzhou are unwilling to sell. Although the sales in foreign firms are quiet, because futures are being settled, the need for spot goods is also strong. The external market is rising sharply. Shenglian and Anli have already opened sales at 18 taels according to foreign regulations, with 100 tons traded. Xiang Tung dealer prices have been hyped up to 17.2 taels. The internal market is also following, with Chunyuan and other brands being wholesaled at 16.6 taels. However, because shipments from downstream are continuing to arrive in Hanzhou, people are inevitably nervous. Sichuan dealers are currently opening prices at 98 taels, and dealer sales are opening at 104 taels for general goods and 102 taels for rice heart. Currently, because the end of the year is approaching, foreign firms lack buying interest, and domestic sales are also trending towards stagnation. The market is flat and uneventful.

Silk and Tea, Sichuan Silk Ends Difficult to Sell at High Costs 141

Local defense forces in Sichuan province are adding surcharges to import and export goods. Yellow and white silk ends exported from Mianzhou, Tongzhou, and other places must all be taxed, resulting in increased costs. Recently, overseas economies have been unstable, and silk end factory sales in Lyon, Marseille, and other places have been sluggish, with prices coming in surprisingly low. General Shanghai merchants are thinking of suppressing prices and hoarding cocoon silk, raw silk handkerchiefs, etc. Although French firms have interest, they are opening prices even lower. Chinese merchants are losing too much, with each dan losing over ten taels to forty or fifty taels. It is difficult to sell, and the market is stagnant, with no one knowing the cost.

Yesterday, the Jinlong foreign firm in the Qimen black tea market bought over 300 boxes, with sales from 31 taels to 34 taels. The market price is extremely low.

Implementing the National Calendar New Year Method 146

The Preparatory Committee for Celebrating the New Year: The Preparatory Committee for Celebrating the National Calendar New Year from all walks of life in this city held its first standing committee meeting yesterday at the City Party Headquarters. Yang Qingyuan of the City Party Headquarters, Hou Dachun, Li Feng, Commander Jiang Yi of the Headquarters, Zheng Chengqing of the City Chamber of Commerce, the City Government, the Citizens' Federation, the Local Court, and other representatives attended. Chairman Hou Dachun performed the ceremony, and then the discussion began to determine the positions and top calculation as follows:

Allocation of positions:

General Affairs Section: Director - City Party Headquarters, City Government, City Chamber of Commerce

Compilation Section: Director - Academic Representative, Deputy Director - Education Bureau, Headquarters

Recreation Department: Director - City Government, Deputy Director - Social Affairs Bureau, City Party Headquarters

Speech Department: Director - Both Road Party Headquarters, Deputy Directors - Each District Party Headquarters

Passing the budget: The preparatory funds are fixed at 3,000 yuan, which will be allocated by various agencies as follows: Printed materials: 990 yuan. Recreation: 990 yuan. General Affairs: 660 yuan. Speech: 90 yuan. Dinner: 210 yuan. Reserve fund: 210 yuan. Next, the discussion decided that groups would participate in the dinner for free, and it was decided that fees would be collected from various agencies today.

City Government: The City Government of this city has formulated several programs to promote National Calendar New Year entertainment and various rituals, which are divided and recorded as follows:

Notice to the National Government: In order to promote the national calendar, the abolition of the old calendar has been repeatedly ordered to the whole country. All of our citizens should absolutely follow it. The citizens of this city were the first to follow the national calendar, but there are still a few people who inevitably continue to use the old calendar. Now that the 19th year is about to end, the new year is already in sight. In order to promote the interest of citizens in promoting the national calendar New Year, this government has specifically stipulated the following measures:

Rituals: (1) All kinds of rituals and entertainments used by the people around the old calendar New Year, such as New Year greetings, group worship, spring banquets, lantern viewing, ribbon tying, and pasting Spring Festival couplets, shall be moved to the vicinity of the National Calendar New Year. (2) New Year's holidays are from January 1st to 4th, and the 5th is the opening day for stores. If the original holidays are insufficient or more than this number, those who do not open on this day may transfer them to the corresponding date of the National Calendar. However, they must not use the Spring Festival or other names to close down at the end of the old calendar year. (3) If there are conventions such as double pay and annual dividends for the business community at the end of the year, they shall be changed to the National Calendar. (4) The civil habit of major cleaning at the end of the old year should be moved to the winter cleaning program on December 15th of the National Calendar. The above-mentioned measures have been issued by this government and notified to the affiliated organizations to be followed. It is hoped that all citizens will implement them consistently in order to comply with the law and achieve the same enjoyment. Attached is the family celebration ceremony for New Year's Eve and New Year's Day: New Year's Eve is a memorial to ancestors. The family gathers with incense and flowers to worship and hang ancestral portraits in the central hall. The memorial ceremony is as follows: (1) Stand at attention. (2) Pay tribute to the ancestors. (3) The head of the family offers flowers. (4) Report (explain the meaning of the memorial, let them know what has been gained in the past year, and point out the ancestral portraits and narrate their teachings and anecdotes that are sufficient to be cautionary). (5) Perform the farewell ceremony (the younger generation bows to the elders). (6) The whole family enjoys a banquet. New Year's Day celebration ceremony is as follows: (1) Stand at attention. (2) Pay respect to the Party Flag and the portrait of the General Manager. (3) Pay tribute to the ancestors. (4) The head of the family gives a speech (explaining the meaning of the New Year's celebration, making sure to know that the New Year begins to work hard on learning and career, and encouraging the family members). (5) Perform the New Year's ceremony (the younger generation pays the New Year's ceremony to the elders and relatives). (6) Give gifts (the elders reward the younger generation with money, food, and stationery). (7) Banquet (8) Entertainment

The Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters Propaganda Department convened a temporary city propaganda conference at 1:00 p.m. yesterday to discuss the celebration of the National Calendar New Year in the 20th year of the Republic of China. Wu Qingyuan (Cai Hongtian), Minister of Propaganda of the City, presided over the ceremony. First, the chairman reported, and then the propaganda commissioners of each district successively reported the propaganda work in their respective districts. After the conclusion, the discussion began: (1) How should the people of this city assist in the celebration of the National Calendar New Year in the 20th year of the Republic of China? The discussion decided: (1) Starting from December 28th, each district's regular lecture hall should lecture on the meaning of promoting the National Calendar (if there is no regular lecture hall, then select a suitable location to hold it). (2) The preparatory committee will hold lectures on promoting the National Calendar for three days from December 28th, 29th, and 30th. The party headquarters of each district should each send four representatives, and the branch offices of each district should each send two representatives to attend the meeting. (3) The permanent propaganda teams of each district branch should set out to publicize on December 28th, 29th, and 30th and convene district propaganda meetings in advance to discuss all proceedings. (4) From December 30th, 31st, New Year's Day, and the 2nd and 3rd for five days, each district should organize music parades to set out and publicize. (5) Areas far from the city such as Jiangwan, Wusong, Pudong, and Meilong should hold recreational gatherings to celebrate. (6) The regular publications of each district should publish New Year special editions. (The rest of the case is omitted.)

Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that the measures for promoting the National Calendar and New Year's holidays have been announced in the City Government's 205th bulletin, and the Bureau and the City Party Headquarters have repeatedly stipulated the disposal measures for unauthorized business closures during the Old Calendar New Year in Bulletins No. 4684 and No. 5096, requiring both labor and capital in industrial and commercial factories to abide by them. The Central Standing Committee has also resolved that all industries must not take holidays during the Old Calendar New Year. According to reports, industry associations such as the money industry and banks have decided to close for five or two days from February 16th to 20th of the 20th year as the final accounting period. Financial institutions are the hub of all industries. Once the market is closed, all industries will inevitably take a break. At that time, it is appropriate to pretend to be using the old calendar under the guise of the end of the year, hindering the promotion of the National Calendar. This Bureau cannot be lenient in enforcing government orders. It is hereby ordered that the Association immediately inform all colleagues to abide by them, and do not take holidays at the end of the old calendar year under the guise of causing disputes.

Zhabei New Power Plant Officially Generates Electricity Today 149

Municipal Public Utilities Bureau Sends Personnel to Supervise

Official Trial Results Satisfactory

For many years, Zhabei Water and Electricity Company has purchased electricity from the Electricity Department of the former Public Concession Bureau and today's Shanghai Power Company and resold it. In order to recover profit rights, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau urged the company to prepare and implement a plan to build its own power plant at Jian Songqiao. Construction of the factory building began in September of the 17th year and included a boiler room, power generation room, management room, switch room, and water intake room. The boilers and machines were purchased from the Czech Skoda factory and installed by them. Installation began in March of the 18th year and was completed in June of the 19th year. However, the trial procedures were complicated and unusual, so electricity has not been formally generated. Formal trials were held on the 18th and 19th of this month. The Public Utilities Bureau sent technical personnel in charge to the site to monitor the No. 1 and No. 2 steam turbine generators. After load testing, speed variation rate testing, and emergency safety valve testing, engineers from the company and the manufacturer were cautious in their work, and the results were quite satisfactory. This kind of formal motor test under the supervision of the official government is still an innovation in China. It is said that the company is now scheduled to formally generate electricity today (the 24th) in the power supply area of the Jiyang Bridge Main Transformer Station, but the power must be turned off for ten minutes during the current exchange period.
