Gao Shuo Files Arbitration Award in the Jinliyuan Case 151

Declares Not Being Restricted by the French Side in Any Way

China Merchants Bureau Has Perpetual Lease Right with Special Permission

Due to the mediation relationship in the Jinliyuan Wharf case of the China Merchants Bureau, the French Consul General Mr. Gangerin requested the China Merchants Bureau to submit the arbitration award as soon as possible. The China Merchants Bureau was afraid of enforcement problems and replied with a refusal. Later, the French Consul General entrusted Mr. Du Yuesheng to explain the good intentions and guaranteed that it would never be enforced. The China Merchants Authority agreed that the arbitrator, lawyer Gao Shuo, would submit the arbitration award. Now, the original manuscript has been found as follows: 1. Arbitration Report: The defendant, China Merchants Bureau, the law firm of arbitrator Gao Shuo, No. 316, Dufu Lane, Fuxu Road, submitted the arbitration opinion on the case of the San De Tang lawsuit against the China Merchants Bureau regarding the land disputes of Aizi No. 69 and Aizi No. 69 in the French Register. In this case, in the midst of mutual mediation, the China Merchants Bureau will not be in the slightest way restricted from its rights to proceed with reconciliation and to file for retrial in the future due to the submission of this arbitration award. This should be stated first. Second, the China Merchants Bureau has a historically specially permitted perpetual lease right to the land on the French Register No. 69 and Aizi No. 69 (see the original deed in Chinese characters for verification). Now, the San De Tang wants to sell the Aizi No. 69 part to the China Merchants Bureau and should not raise the price to as much as 390,000 taels. The French Public Works Bureau estimates that the land price is only worth 128,436 taels of silver. This should be stated second. Third, if the China Merchants Bureau follows the mediator's opinion and allows the San De Tang to take back its time problem, it should be based on the precedent of the San De Tang first signing a contract with the China Merchants Bureau in 1890 and not fully handing over the house until 1892. This time, the handover should also be extended by two years, so that the China Merchants Bureau can calmly arrange the stack room and the relocation of tenants. This should be stated third. In addition, the valuation of warehouses and civil houses at No. 69 can be done separately by inviting engineering experts to make a detailed valuation at that time. This matter is temporarily reserved. This should be stated fourth. Since the China Merchants Bureau continues to occupy the two plots of land, the rent should still be paid in full by the China Merchants Bureau in accordance with the original contract to show fairness. This arbitrator presents the above respectfully based on what he has seen. If the Jun Court has any further questions, he will be ready to obey orders at any time. This is respectfully presented to the French Concession Joint Court. December 13th, the 19th year of the Republic of China. China Merchants Bureau arbitrator Gao Shuo. ) This document was personally handed over by lawyer Gao Shuo to Du Huadong Yuesheng for forwarding and is currently under negotiation. In the future, the French Consul General and Mr. She may be able to mediate a peaceful solution.

City Public Security Bureau Strictly Forbids Pujiang Bandits from Harassing Passengers 152

Requesting Assistance from the Shipping Guild

Forwarding to Various Shipping Companies for Suppression

Shanghai is a major port for commerce, with dozens of large and small ships entering the port every day. The various gangs of bandits in the Huangpu River are countless. Therefore, passengers coming to Shanghai from various places often suffer unexpected financial losses or sacrifice their time when encountering these lawless elements, and some even face the threat of death. Although the Municipal Public Security Bureau has made every effort to suppress and arrest them, the results have not been effective. Recently, the Municipal Public Security Bureau received a request from the Shanghai Travelers' Association to take strict measures to suppress them in order to ensure the safety of travelers. After considering the situation, the Public Security Bureau sent a letter to the Shanghai Shipping Guild requesting them to forward it to the various shipping companies, asking them to assist the water police in preventing this when ships arrive in Shanghai. The letter is recorded as follows:

Public Security Bureau to the Shipping Guild, greetings: The Shanghai Travelers' Association reported that the members of the association, such as Tai'an Inn, reported that bandits had accumulated along the Huangpu River port area for a long time, becoming the only way to harass traveling merchants. They often impersonate staff members of various inns, making it unpredictable. Passengers arriving at this port are inevitably subject to unexpected losses, so everyone is cautious. At noon on the 22nd of this month, the Fengyang Maru arrived at the port, and Chen Jian, a regular customer of a small inn from Guangdong, brought one family member and twelve pieces of luggage. The bandits coveted the luggage, and five or six people impersonated staff members of the small inn and forcibly took the luggage down to the rowing boat. When they arrived on the shore, they encountered Zhang Zhenmao, the real receptionist of the small inn, who exposed the bandits. The bandits immediately threatened the passenger to prevent him from making a fuss and surrounded Zhang Zhenmao, using force and beating him in the abdomen and other places, pushing him down by the side of the road. A horse-drawn cart ran over the passenger. It is well-known that Yingzhou Hotel, belonging to the passenger's uncle, extorted twelve yuan under the pretext of transporting luggage. Fortunately, the passenger gave them the money in full before they were released. In addition to the injured Zhang Zhenmao reporting to the water police, we earnestly request your association to immediately submit a report to the authorities for strict suppression in order to eliminate the harm to travelers. Furthermore, the sixteen major hotels, including Dongfang, Mengyuan, Shenzhou, Xiangbin, Yuandong, Juelu, Dachina, and Xintiandi, jointly sent a letter stating that the Pujiang bandits harass travelers, harming them day and night, and requesting the government to quickly eliminate them, etc. After reviewing the situation, it was found that the various ports along the Huangpu River have always been a gathering place for bandits. There are secret organizations such as the Thirty-Six Gang and the Twenty-Eight Gang, known as the source of evil. They either impersonate receptionists of various inns or disguise themselves as porters of various shipping companies, trying to get close to passengers and engage in deception. Passengers who unfortunately fall victim to their schemes suffer small losses of money and luggage, and large losses of people and children. Moreover, these gang rowing bandits often take advantage of the moment when the ship is about to enter the port and has not completely stopped, rushing up with hooks in groups and forcibly snatching passengers' luggage and descending. Even if passengers are skilled in traveling, it is difficult to take care of everything in the midst of such chaos and complexity. The most hateful thing is when they encounter single passengers or passengers with a lot of luggage, they will stop the boat in the middle of the river and demand exorbitant prices. If they do not get what they want, they will curse and refuse to sail. During the day, they only rock the boat and create danger deliberately. At night, they even kill people. Such situations are too numerous to mention, and newspapers have reported countless cases. There are countless more that are not reported in the newspapers. As a result, most people in society regard traveling on the waterway of the Sixteenth Pier as a dangerous road. The bandits are densely distributed on the ports, no different from a tiger's mouth. Not only do countless merchants and ordinary people complain about their travels, but I believe that officials at all levels have also unfortunately experienced it firsthand and lamented the difficulty of the road to Shu. The harm caused by the Pujiang bandits is only local, and they must impersonate legitimate porters when approaching travelers, which is not difficult to distinguish. It is not difficult to investigate and arrest them. Why is it that these petty thieves have not been eliminated to this day? If they are allowed to do evil for a long time, the harm will eventually become severe. Travelers are constantly suffering disasters. Is this the blessing of local security? Moreover, Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreign travelers pass through, and the world pays attention to it. If the guards are not sufficient, it is easy to give people an excuse. The interests of the members of the association are deeply related to the business of traveling merchants. It is inconvenient to remain silent in the face of danger. According to the reports from various hotels, we request a strict suppression of the above-mentioned situation. Therefore, we respectfully request your bureau to review and expedite the following: (1) Supervise and order the water and land police to strictly investigate and arrest the gang rowing bandits at the ports, punish them according to the law, parade them in the streets to deter their source.

Page 14

(2) Instruct the various shipping companies to strictly prohibit the hooking and rowing boats from climbing up and forcibly snatching passengers' luggage when the ships enter the port and have not stopped, in order to prevent incidents and avoid danger. Otherwise, the shipping company should be responsible, or follow the example of Japanese ships and issue permits for boarding the ships, cutting off their way. (3) Allow the association and various hotels to request voluntary police protection for business travelers at their own expense to improve the situation. If these three points can be achieved, the harm of the port bandits can be cleared, the local security can be relied on for a long time, the traveling merchants can enjoy the benefits, and the traffic will be in order. We earnestly request your approval for implementation. Countless travelers will be grateful, etc. Based on this, it was found that the rowing bandits, that is, the Thirty-Six Gang, had previously been ordered to be suppressed by the water patrol team within a limited time due to the investigation of the harassment of travelers. Now, the report shows that the rowing bandits are still rampant, which is really reckless. In addition to ordering the water patrol team to investigate and strictly deal with the matter and issue instructions, we should also send a letter to your association to inform the various shipping companies to strictly prohibit the hooking of ships by rowing boats in the Huangpu River and the forced interception of passengers' luggage, in order to ensure the safety of travelers and maintain security. We hope to receive a reply for reference, etc. After receiving the letter, the Shipping Guild sent letters to the various shipping companies, saying:

Shipping Guild Notice to Various Shipping Companies, greetings: We have received a public letter from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau regarding the investigation and prohibition of bandits in the Huangpu River from harassing passengers. We are instructed to immediately inform the various shipping companies to strictly prohibit the hooking of ships by rowing boats in the Huangpu River and the forced interception of passengers' luggage, in order to ensure the safety of travelers and maintain security, etc. Therefore, we have urgently recorded and printed the original letter and sent it to you. Please review it and inform the various shipping companies to comply with it. Sincerely, Shanghai Shipping Guild. Attached is a copy of the original letter from the Public Security Bureau.

Garrison Headquarters Yesterday Issued a Notice 153

Revoking the Previous Notice of the Dock Cargo Storage Company The Songhu Garrison Headquarters issued a notice yesterday, saying: Regarding the matter of issuing a notice, the Shanghai Municipal Government has consulted, stating that the Finance Bureau, Social Bureau, Public Security Bureau, Public Works Bureau, and Port Affairs Bureau have jointly submitted a request. The request stated that the Shanghai Dock Cargo Storage Company was found to have extorted money from sick merchants and had been jointly submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to revoke the company's license and order it to cease operations. The Municipal Government issued Directive No. 7715, approving the transfer of the consultation, etc. The Municipal Public Security Bureau complied with the order and informed the various districts and ordered strict suppression and maintenance. The Finance Bureau also reported that the personnel of the Pu Zhao River Ship Donation Inspection Office were still forcibly demanding insurance donations from boat owners. The Finance Bureau convened a meeting on the 8th of this month to discuss the matter again and decided that, in addition to complying with the directive and ordering the various districts and offices of the Public Security Bureau to strictly suppress the matter, the Finance Bureau may at any time send the company's personnel to the competent district office of the Public Security Bureau for handling if the above-mentioned situation is found again. At the same time, the Finance Bureau will first submit a joint request to the Municipal Government to forward it to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to revoke the previous notice issued to the company. The Public Security Bureau and the Social Bureau jointly received Directive No. 6411 from the Municipal Government, which was forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which replied that the company had been ordered to dissolve and ordered to surrender its license. In addition to ordering the various district offices and the Water Patrol Team of the Public Security Bureau to order the dissolution of all the offices established by the company and report the matter, and ordering the Social Bureau to limit the company to surrender the original registration license by a certain date, and then submitting another document for forwarding to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, all the original requests of the bureaus, such as the request to forward the consultation to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to revoke the notice, were jointly submitted for review and forwarding. According to this investigation, the Shanghai Dock Cargo Storage Company has been extorting money from sick businesses, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has approved the order to dissolve the company and ordered the company to submit the original registration certificate. In addition to the order to forward the consultation, we hereby inform you that we will promptly revoke the previously issued notice and request a reply.

Hope for Resolution of Liquor Trade Strike 154

The Director of the First District Acts as Mediator

The Labor's Demands Are Accepted by the Management

The strike in the liquor trade in this city has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, Huang Zhenbo, Director of the Tobacco and Liquor Affairs Bureau of the Second District, felt that it would not be good if the strike could not be resolved, so he took the initiative to mediate. The situation yesterday is reported as follows:

Labor Congress Yesterday at 2:00 p.m., the labor union held its sixth member congress. Gu Jiren was elected as chairman and the meeting began with the usual formalities. The agenda was discussed as follows: (1) The management has telegraphed the provincial bureau to accuse the union of this strike. What attitude should the union take? It was decided that (A) the union should support the management in collecting evidence of the fine to plan for action; (B) the union should also negotiate with the office separately. (2) A letter should be sent to the sauce and liquor trade association to temporarily suspend the delivery of white liquor during the strike. The resolution was passed.

Trade Association Meeting The trade association held a member congress at 4:00 p.m. yesterday. Chairman Huang Yuming began the meeting with the usual formalities. The chairman first reported that the strike negotiation had been convened by Huang Zhenbo, Director of the Tobacco and Liquor Affairs Bureau of the Second District, to mediate between the two sides, but no agreement had yet been reached. The agenda was then discussed: (1) Continue to submit a report to the provincial bureau and the Second District Branch Bureau to investigate Ben Guangzhen; (2) Send representatives to the Second District Branch Bureau to petition. If there is no result, submit a report to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance for investigation; (3) Never stop the action until the goal of canceling the time limit is achieved.

Labor Negotiations At 4:00 p.m. yesterday, the labor union sent representatives Hu Gujun, Xu Ziyi, and Wang Ade to the inspection office to request the conditions of the labor from Director Li Guangzhen. Director Li sincerely received and explained, saying that the stamping of the seal was a procedure to rectify tax collection, and the office would naturally sympathize with and pay attention to the convenience of the labor. The reasons for the requested conditions were sufficient and completely accepted. The time for stamping the seal would also be extended to six hours later for those who exceeded the limit. However, the office could not accept the request to limit the time for stamping the seal and the request for compensation for the loss of work. The labor representatives immediately returned to the union and agreed to formally sign a contract for further contact this afternoon. The mediation of Director Huang also yielded considerable results and may be resolved today.

Director Li's Talk Director Li Guangzhen of the inspection office told a reporter from the Huadong News Agency yesterday that the office has accepted several conditions proposed by the labor for the sake of the labor. However, it is difficult to cancel the time stamp on the seal, because the office has seen that merchants intentionally take advantage of loopholes and affix seals that are not in use. In order to rectify the state tax revenue, the office has affixed the date stamp on the original seal and ordered merchants to affix it themselves when the liquor leaves the door to prevent tax evasion. All the detailed measures have been reported to the district branch bureau, the municipal social bureau, and the municipal public security bureau for the record, etc.

It is also reported that Director Guan of the Jiangsu Provincial Tobacco and Liquor Affairs Bureau has sent Section Chief Xue to Shanghai to thoroughly investigate the strike.

Commander Xiong's Condition Gradually Improves 155

He Yingqin Visited Him Yesterday

Yang Yongtai Sent a Letter of Condolence

Commander Xiong's condition has been good since he was admitted to the orthopaedic hospital, but he has a slight cough and his body temperature is often around 38 degrees Celsius. It is reported that Dr. Niu Huisheng and the president of Baolong Hospital consulted the night before and used a certain drug injection, which was very effective. Yesterday, his body temperature dropped to around 36 degrees Celsius, which was no different from a normal person. His spirit was better and his appetite gradually increased. Since being admitted to the hospital, Commander Xiong's left hand and right foot have been clamped with boards, and he has not been able to turn over for half a month. His pain can be imagined. The doctor was afraid that his conversation would hurt his spirit, so he did not allow even close relatives to talk to him. It is reported that Xiong said to a certain officer under his command that he would listen to the doctor's words and strictly abide by the rules. Although his illness was painful, his heart was strong. However, lying flat for half a month and not being able to move sometimes felt like being dead. The pain was only bearable to him. He was injured while suppressing bandits, and now the bandits are still rampant and the suffering of the people has not been eliminated. His own pain is so unbearable that he did not expect it, etc. Those who heard his words should all sympathize with him. His injury is not only a misfortune for Xiong himself. Those who visited him yesterday included He Yingqin, Minister of Military and Political Affairs, and Liu Jiwen, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs. Yang Yongtai's condition has also gradually improved. Yesterday, he sent a special letter to express his condolences to Xiong. The letter from him to Xiong is as follows (Tianyi, my brother, is now able to get up and write with effort. Before writing to my brother, I would like to silently mourn for one minute for the colleagues who died in the plane crash. There were seven people on board that day, and only you and I are left. I heard that your injuries are in your left hand and right foot, which is more serious than mine. I am very concerned. I only injured two ribs on my left side, and the blood on my left side has not completely dissipated. I think Drs. Gu and Ding have already told you in detail. The doctor said that after half a month of rest, everything will definitely recover. The past few days have been good, and I have been sleeping and eating well. I am writing to comfort you. If the situation permits this year, and I recover my walking first, I will definitely visit your residence to see your injuries. This is the second time that my brother and I have faced danger together. During the May 3rd Massacre a few years ago, we were trapped in the Jinan Governor's Office and suddenly encountered enemy planes dropping bombs within ten steps. Eight people were killed, but you and I were sitting at a table, eating and talking, and we were safe. In this battle, five of the seven people on board died, and you and I are still the only two left. Twice we could have died together, but we did not die. Is it because God has repeatedly favored us, or is it because we still have a small responsibility to the party and the country to the society that has not been completed, and we still need to work together with the spirit of dying together to make greater concerted efforts? The coincidence of the opportunity is deeply impressed, and the friendship will never be forgotten. I deeply hope that we will build on the previous cause and seek good results, and open up the future life. I only hope that we can help each other and encourage each other. I hereby send this message and wish you a speedy recovery. Your brother, Yang Yongtai, on the sickbed of Baolong Hospital, December 22nd.

Ministry of Finance Tax Administration Admonishes Subordinates 157

Should Pay Attention to Six Points

The Ministry of Finance Tax Administration issued an order to its subordinate bureaus to pay attention to the key points. The order was to comply with the matter, stating that the establishment of the unified tax system is based on the principle of increasing national income and facilitating merchants, collecting taxes once at the district where goods are produced and imported. Except for imported goods, which are still subject to customs duties, after the unified tax is paid, it can be circulated without obstruction and any tax or fee is exempt from double taxation. If there is an error in taxation, a refund will be allowed. There are regulations and laws that are very well prepared. For example, since the reform of the unified tax on cigarettes, the tax revenue has increased day by day and merchants have found it convenient. With success already achieved, the Ministry has recently issued an order to approve the abolition of Likin on January 1 next year. All cotton yarn, matches, and cement will be changed to the unified tax and will be managed by the Ministry along with cigarettes and wheat flour. The Minister has been in business for a long time and knows deeply that merchants are suffering from heavy taxes and the difficulties of bureaus. This time, the Minister has been ordered to preside over the matter. First, the provincial bureaus will be divided into district bureaus and management offices will be set up in the factory areas. The original inspection offices will be retained or abolished separately. As the reorganization is just beginning, the key points that should be paid attention to are listed below: (1) The staff will be transferred by the Ministry from time to time, and every effort should be made to ensure that they are capable and make the most of their strengths, using one person to achieve the effect of one person. (2) This reorganization of the Ministry only seeks old staff. It will never be changed easily unless it is absolutely necessary, but it must be competent, make the best use of its talents, and allocate work at any time to apply it. In the future, there will be separate reward and punishment methods to protect the employment of staff. (3) The Ministry will assess the merits and demerits. If the performance is excellent, promotion will be allowed. (4) Private gain and fraud must be punished. Merchants should be allowed to report confidentially at any time. If there is any solicitation of bribes or obstruction, once the facts are verified, there will be no leniency. (5) If it is not necessary to establish an inspection office, the office should consider the situation and abolish it to avoid the problem of obstruction at every level. (6) The director and deputy director of the bureau should be jointly responsible for the performance of their duties and should not follow the previous practice of having a nominal director. The level of work in each district bureau and the diligence, competence, and incompetence of the staff will still be assessed by the Ministry's inspectors, who will go to each district at any time to conduct inspections and personally inspect them to see the results and emphasize the tax policy. All these points should be encouraged together. We must know that to promote benefits, we must first eliminate abuses, and to cultivate ourselves, we must lead our subordinates. We must clear up all the old tax malpractices from the past so that business can develop and tax revenue can increase. We must save on expenses so that we can reduce costs and compete with the achievements of customs and salt affairs. The Minister's responsibility is to lead by example, and the directors of each bureau and the principal staff should be willing to work together to encourage each other so that the policy of benefiting the country and the people will not be in vain. In addition to issuing an order, the directors (director and deputy director of the bureau) (director and deputy director of the office) should all comply with it and report the date of receipt of the document for investigation. This order.

The Chinese Jisheng Society recently received a distress letter from Taihu County, Anhui Province, regarding a bandit robbery and request for relief. The letter stated that Taihu is located in the western border of Anhui Province, neighboring Huangsuwang. Last year, it suffered from the disturbance of Yu Yanong, and the people were still in shock. This summer, it was disturbed by the remnants of Han Jie, and the entire city was looted, causing great damage to its vitality. Unexpectedly, on November 16th, a group of over two thousand communists from Huangmei, Hubei Province, suddenly attacked and captured our county town. They killed our fellow villagers and town leaders, robbed our goods, burned our tools, incited our ignorant people, kidnapped our students, arbitrarily damaged government offices and schools, and ransacked stores of all sizes, burning documents, books, and grain. They transported away clothes, bedding, and silver. The catastrophe of Changsha was played out in the small town of Taihu. Alas! The bandits have fled far away, and the people have gradually gathered, but most of the ashes are rotten. Fathers cry out for their sons, husbands grieve for their wives, there is no grain to eat, no clothes to wear, no mats to sit on, no beds to sleep on, no cooking utensils, no lamps or fire. The vitality of the hundred-mile Taihu Mountain has waned, and hunger and cold are imminent in the cold winter. There has never been a catastrophe greater than this. If the benevolent people of the world, with a broad and compassionate heart, share our pain and suffering, and offer food and clothing or distribute wealth, and pour out the water of benevolence to revive the parched lands, then…

Local News Two

National Goods Bank General Manager Zhu Chengzhang Kidnapped Yesterday Morning, Escaped Late at Night 169

Automobile Driver Wang Amao Died Tragically

Zhu's Beloved Daughter Runzhu Hit by Three Bullets

Female Nurse Injured in Left Hand by Stray Bullet

Zhu Slightly Uncomfortable, Resting Quietly in the Hospital

The Kidnappers' Automobile Permit Was Found to be Forged

Zhu Chengzhang, General Manager of the China National Goods Bank, was kidnapped by bandits near his residence on Yuyuan Road yesterday morning. The driver was shot and killed by the bandits. Zhu's daughter and a female nurse were injured by stray bullets. After the bandits kidnapped Zhu, they immediately bundled him into a car parked by the roadside and sped away. After neighbors reported the incident to the police station by telephone, the bandits had already gone far away without a trace. There were six people in Zhu's car, one was kidnapped, one was killed, and two were injured. This is truly a tragic incident among the recent kidnapping cases.

Bandits Open Fire on Zhu Chengzhang Zhu Chengzhang lives in a Western-style house at No. 189, opposite Yuyuan New Village on Yuyuan Road. At around 9:40 yesterday morning, Zhu was traveling in his own car, No. 10340, driven by the driver Tu Amao. In addition to the master and servant, Zhu's daughter Runzhu, Zhu's wife's nurse Ms. Deng, and the driver's assistant Wu Linsheng and tea servant Jiang Laitao were also in the car, a total of six people. Zhu got into the car and ordered Amao to drive. Who knew that before they had gone far, a car suddenly blocked the road ahead, making it difficult for the driver Wang Amao to advance or retreat. As he did not know how to offend the other party, bullets flew towards him, striking him incessantly. Amao was shot and fell in the driver's seat.

Zhu Was Kidnapped, Daughter Injured, Why the Bullets?

It turned out that they were fired by the kidnappers as a prelude to kidnapping Zhu Chengzhang. As the gunpowder smoke cleared, the car door suddenly opened, and two bandits jumped into the car, dragged Zhu out of the car, and sped away in the bandits' car in a flash. Zhu's daughter, Ms. Runzhu, was sitting next to her father and was hit by a stray bullet. Her companion, Ms. Deng, was also injured by gunfire. Thus, four of the six people in the car suffered, and only Wu and Jiang, who were sitting with the driver, were unscathed. However, they were so terrified that they were like wooden chickens.

Neighbors Report to the Police Station Zhu's residence is in a very secluded area near Yuyuan Road. At the sound of gunfire, the neighbors were shocked and immediately reported to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station. The Chinese and Western detectives drove to the scene, but the bandits' car had long disappeared. The driver Wang Amao, who was shot, died from his injuries. Zhu's daughter Runzhu and the female nurse were sent to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. Ms. Zhu was hit by three bullets, one of which pierced her abdomen and grazed her liver, and the other two were in her left and right arms, which were not seriously injured. The nurse Deng was injured in her left hand, which was less serious.

Purchasing Christmas Gifts Zhu is a 47-year-old Anhui native and a Christian. He has been working in the banking industry for many years and has a wide circle of friends in Shanghai. His daughter Runzhu is 17 years old and is studying at the McTyeire School. Zhu's wife, Ms. Huang, has been ill for a long time and has been bedridden for several months. Ms. Deng is her nurse. Recently, Ms. Huang's illness has slightly improved, so she instructed her beloved daughter Runzhu to accompany her father in the car to purchase winter solstice gifts and planned to set up a Christmas tree at home tonight to celebrate. Therefore, the father and daughter were very happy when they went out, not expecting that disaster was imminent and that such a huge misfortune would occur only a few steps away from their home.

Blood Stains on the Cushion Zhu's residence is on Yuyuan Road, not far from HOTELTINY. To enter from Yuyuan Road, one must pass through a private road, in the center of which is a circular flowerbed. Cars going east and west circle around the garden. Therefore, when Zhu's car was going out, it was heading west and north. The bandits' car was parked between the flowerbed and the wall, blocking Zhu's car's progress. Two bandits were also left to the east of the flowerbed. When Zhu's car approached, it was difficult to advance or retreat. When Zhu was dragged out of the car, there were many blood stains left on the seat cushion. It is also a question whether Zhu was shot. The number of bandits was about five or six, half of whom were armed with guns.

The Bandits' Car Had a Fake Permit The license plate number of the bandits' car was 7732, which was also seen by a neighbor and reported to the police station. However, according to a later investigation, the car permit was forged. Zhu's car is a sedan-style foreign blue car. Several pieces of the window glass were broken by bullets. There were blood stains on the driver's seat cushion and the car seat cushion.

The Court Inspects the Corpse The scene of the incident was originally in the Chinese Concession, but because Yuyuan Road was built beyond the boundary, the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives in police cars to search in all directions after the incident. However, after Ren, the district chief of the Caoxi Road Sixth District Public Security Bureau, heard the news, he immediately led Inspector Xu and others to investigate. The Public Security Bureau's Third Section reported the corpse of the driver Wang Amao to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Wu Shixin and Detective Xuan Zhiming were appointed to conduct the autopsy.

Mr. Zhu Escaped Last Night This newspaper received further news at 2:00 AM this morning that Mr. Zhu escaped from the bandits' den at around 11:00 PM last night. He suffered minor injuries and was accompanied to Baolong Hospital for treatment, then transferred to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road. Mr. Zhu is in good spirits, and his relatives and friends must be pleasantly surprised to hear the news.

Lu Shaotang Escaped 170

French Concession Arrested Criminals

Confessed that the Ticket Was Hidden on Hart Road

Lu Shaotang, a native of Suzhou, lives at No. 235, Daqing Lane, Jiujiang Road. He is a real estate businessman with a good reputation in Shanghai, which made him coveted by kidnapping bandits. On the 29th of this month, that is, last Friday evening at 6:30, he was kidnapped by bandits at the corner of Nanjing Road and Yunnan Road. His Russian bodyguard was shot and killed on the spot by the bandits for protecting his master. After this incident occurred, the Public Concession Police Department paid close attention. After Chinese Detective Lu Liankui purchased information and investigated in many ways, he arrested several criminals related to the case in the French Concession on Lafayette Road yesterday. They confessed that the ticket was hidden at No. 374 Hart Road in the Public Concession. The Chinese and Western detectives of the Old Gate Police Station went to the address fully armed and rescued Lu. At that time, there were two people guarding the ticket. Because they were outnumbered, Lu escaped safely. However, he had been in the bandits' den for four days and suffered a great deal of mental stimulation.

Xiao Xin'an Will Return Home 171

Ms. Xiao Xin'an from Yixing was hired by the Pede School on Ambon Island in the Dutch East Indies and traveled far across the ocean, suffering a major insult from the first and second mates of the Dutch liner Chepad of the Java Company. All sectors of the country were filled with righteous indignation and jointly offered assistance. According to reliable information, Ms. Xiao has decided to return home after the Pede School has scheduled a winter vacation to begin on the 30th of this month, in order to inform all sectors of the country about the truth of the matter. She has already sent a letter to friends in Shanghai yesterday.

Foreign Ships Collide 172

Caused by Tidal Surge

The Shanghai Evening Post reported that at around 11:00 this morning (the 23rd), two ships in the Huangpu River were suddenly agitated by the tide and brushed past the Libang ship, which was moored between the sixth and seventh pontoons, breaking the mooring line. The Libang ship then drifted with the tide, causing its stern to graze the Pacific Ocean telecommunications cable ship of the Great Northern Telegraph Company, breaking its pontoon mooring line. The Pacific Ocean ship also drifted to the Datong Wharf in Pudong and struck the Japanese freighter Takayama Maru (transliteration), destroying its right railing and steel plate. Fortunately, the Libang ship had managed to drop both left and right anchors by this time, but when it dropped anchor, it collided with the seventh pontoon. The Pacific Ocean ship also dropped anchor and was able to stop drifting. However, the names of the two ships that caused the initial disaster had not been determined by the afternoon. It is said that one ship was the Swedish ship Niagara, but this has not been confirmed. The total amount of losses will be estimated by experts.

The Chinese Society Photography Exhibition Closed Yesterday 173

Exhibition in Beijing on January 4th

Yesterday was the last day of the Chinese Society Photography Exhibition. A small number of new works, such as those by Chen Shanshan, were replaced and displayed. There were about 2,000 visitors, including the Shandong Normal School visiting group and various organizations. Although the works of the American Ge Siding were in a guest position, many Chinese painters came to the exhibition and praised his skills. The exhibition closed at 6:00 PM, but some people still lingered at the venue. At 7:00 PM, all members of the Chinese Society held a New Year's dinner party at Quanjiafu Restaurant and elected new officials for the twentieth year. The society also received letters from the Capital Xinjing Daily, the Municipal Party Department, and a certain educational institution, inviting them to hold an exhibition in Beijing. The meeting decided that the exhibition would be held publicly in Beijing on January 4th of the twentieth year and immediately sent a telegram to members in Beijing, such as Huang Zhenyu and Shi Xinjia, to prepare nearby.

The Case of the Tragic Death of the School Servant at Tongwen College Was Reported Yesterday 174

Widow and Orphans' Voices Full of Tears

The case of the tragic death of Li Hailin, a school servant at Tongwen College, has been seen in various newspapers in recent days. The family members of the deceased are young, and only Li's wife is supporting herself after childbirth. Therefore, the Japanese have repeatedly intimidated her after Li's death, and forced Li's wife to cry and move the body out of the school on the afternoon of the previous day (the 21st), without mentioning any follow-up measures, with the intention of eliminating the problem. Although Li's wife led a group of orphans and pleaded for compensation with tears, the Japanese unilaterally verbally agreed to give 800 yuan, without mentioning the cost of Li's wife's old age and the living expenses and education of the children. However, Li still has brothers in his ancestral home in Hubei. When he heard the news of Li's death, he was extremely angry and has recently set out to Shanghai to negotiate. More than 60 Chinese servants in the school also believe that Li's case is unjustified and that the Japanese usually treat Chinese servants harshly. In order to help Li's case and demand improved treatment, they have initiated the organization of a school workers' union. In addition, the Li case support association organized by Chinese in the school has decided to do everything in its power to help Li's family to achieve the conditions of dismissing and punishing the perpetrators of the tragic case and providing compensation and follow-up measures.

Jiangnan Steamer Collides 175

Sank at Datong Wharf in the River Bottom

At around 6:00 the night before last, the Jiangnan Steamer of the Jiangnan Shipyard was heading north from the shipyard wharf. Near the Datong Wharf in Nanshi, it was met head-on by the Minsheng Steamer, which was speeding from the north. There was no time to avoid it, and the bow of the Minsheng steamer crashed into the middle section of the right side of the Jiangnan Steamer. The ship was immediately damaged, and water poured in, threatening to sink it. The Minsheng steamer tied a rope to it and tried to tow it to the Datong Wharf to dock, but when it was nearly a hundred feet from the shore, the Jiangnan Steamer was full of water and immediately sank to the bottom of the river. The sailors were transferred to other ships and were not drowned. After the incident, the captain of the sunken ship, Gu Baosheng, reported it to the water police station for investigation and compensation for losses from the company of the ship that caused the accident.

Coal Boat Hits Rice Boat 176

Hou Jintang Fell into the River with No Way Out

Hou Jintang, a rice boat from Changxi, carried 180 dan of rice to Shanghai. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday and docked at Caojiadu. Hou took the rice samples and left the boat to entrust them to a rice dealer. Hou was standing on the bow of the boat, about to jump onto the dock, when he was violently struck by a barge of the Ren Da Hang, which was fully loaded with coal and heading west. Hou was knocked into the river. There was no way to rescue him on the spot. The barge has now been detained for negotiation. Hou's boat was also smashed at the bow and flooded, causing considerable losses.

Hong Jiangcheng Sand Ship Robbed 177

The Ship Owner Was Kidnapped and Two Crew Members Were Killed

Cargo Was Searched, Injured Were Sent to Hospital

The Hong Longcheng sand ship from Beikou was loaded with soybean oil and northern goods worth more than 40,000 taels of silver on its return to Shanghai from Dalian. When it sailed to the Qingkou Sea, it suddenly encountered a large gang of bandits sailing towards them in four or five pirate ships. They opened fire and ordered the ship to stop. When the crew saw this, they turned the rudder and retreated to avoid danger, but the pirate ships chased after them and continued to open fire. Four or five members of the Hong ship's crew were injured by bullets. At this point, the crew members were frightened, but the pirates continued to chase and eventually caught up with them. The pirates swarmed onto the ship, armed with guns or great force, and struck people indiscriminately, injuring another six or seven people. The pirates searched everywhere, broke open a leather suitcase in the ship owner Luo's room, took out more than 600 yuan in small silver coins and more than 400 yuan in copper coins, more than ten account books from the sand ship, and freight invoices, threw all the account books into the sea, and were still not satisfied. They searched all the crew members and robbed all the silver coins on their bodies, without exception. Before leaving, they kidnapped the ship owner Luo and two crew members and said that they would prepare ransom money and redeem them within ten days. The pirates drove the ship and fled to the East China Sea. The Hong ship is now sailing to Fushan and has docked. The injured crew members have been sent to the hospital for treatment. Two crew members died due to their injuries. The ship immediately purchased coffins and collected the bodies, and sent crew members to Shanghai to report to the cargo numbers and ask them to find a way to rescue the kidnapped ship owner and the other two men. The cargo numbers have telegraphed the local authorities to strictly suppress the bandits and ensure the safety of shipping.

False Alarm, Armed Police Arrived 178

An Incident at Longmao Money Shop

The Wusong Public Security Seventh District Office received an emergency report at around 7:00 last night from the No. 2 alarm bell of the Longmao Money Shop on Songxing Road. District Chief Yang Maorong immediately dispatched Patrol Officer Dai Guosheng and Li Nong, along with more than 20 detectives and armed police officers, to the scene to surround the area. The traffic at the nearby Nanchang Road, Zhongxin Road, and Wenchang Road was temporarily cut off. Then the patrol officers and police officers entered the building to search, but the employees of the shop were calm and nothing was happening. They were suddenly frightened by the sudden arrival of the armed police officers and wondered what had happened. After Patrol Officer Dai and others explained their purpose, they realized that there had been a misunderstanding. No one knew who had pressed the alarm bell, and no one admitted to it. At that time, nearby shops closed their doors one after another and suffered a great shock. The alarm was not lifted until the police officers withdrew. District Chief Yang believes that the alarm bell is important and should not be pressed randomly, so he notified the shop that they should be extra careful in the future to avoid misunderstandings and hindering public order.

Unnamed Male Corpse in Abandoned Field 179

In the abandoned field on the east side of Xingjia Road, Zhabei, at the eastern end of Xingjiazhai Road, Zhabei, an unnamed male corpse was found at around 7:00 yesterday morning. The deceased was about twenty years old, wearing a black cloth short shirt and pants, black cloth shoes, and a bald head. There was one wound on the head caused by a sharp weapon, two wounds on the left side of the neck, and one wound on the right side of the neck. Two axes were found next to the corpse, indicating that he was killed at the scene. The Fifth District First Branch ordered an investigation and found no family members to report it to the Public Security Bureau. It also ordered Ji Yi Tu's local official Yan Liugen to submit it to the local court for an autopsy. After Prosecutor Xuan and the autopsy team arrived for the autopsy, they instructed the hall to collect the body for burial and took the murder weapons back to the treasury for investigation.

Page 16

British Consulate Staff Embezzled 180

Sold a Large Number of Stamps

Sentenced to 30 Days Imprisonment

The British Consulate is busy with affairs and diligent in reporting news. Every day, dozens of letters are mailed to domestic and foreign locations, and a Ningbo native, Le Cangbai, is hired to handle the affairs. The monthly postal expenses are more than 100 yuan. However, since June, the expenses have increased significantly. In the past, the monthly cost was about 110 to 120 yuan, but in July it increased to 150 yuan, and in August it increased to 153 yuan. The Consul, Mr. Packer, who also concurrently serves as a juror at the Mixed Court, is very honest. He saw that the postal expenses increased monthly, but the number of letters sent did not increase. Although the post office increased the postage for letters sent overseas from July, it should not have been such a large increase. Therefore, from September 1st, he began to handle the mailing duties himself. The expenses for that month were only 115 yuan, and the expenses for October and November were only 110 to 120 yuan. However, Mr. Bao was busy with affairs and could not always take care of the mailing duties, so he recently ordered Le to paste the stamps. To prevent him from embezzling, he was instructed to paste the stamps in the same room under supervision. However, Le's deceptive mind was very clever. He first fabricated several envelopes, mixed them into the letters to be sent, and asked Bao for stamps to paste them one by one. Taking advantage of the opportunity to send them to the post office, he removed the stamps pasted on the fake letters and sold them to others. This kind of trick was not easy to detect. Therefore, the postal expenses required this month increased again, averaging one yuan more per day than the previous month. Bao suspected it and paid special attention to it. The day before yesterday afternoon, Le brought four letters to Bao's office and asked for stamps. After Bao examined them, he inquired about the dispatching officer who wrote on the envelope. The truth was revealed, and he immediately telegraphed the Chief Patrol Station to send Western detective Mei Sheng to arrest Le. Together with the four fabricated letters, Le was escorted to the local court of the Special District yesterday. Consul Bao also appeared in court to testify. According to the trial by Judge Xu, Le confessed that he was afraid that Consul Bao would blame him for the inappropriate postal expenses in the past and would be suspended from his position. Therefore, he started to cheat yesterday, hoping to get more money and begged for leniency. Judge Xu sentenced him to 30 days imprisonment and confiscated the fabricated envelopes.

Fire at Scissor Bridge Road 183

There is a rubber factory with a large scale on Scissor Bridge Road behind the local court, which has been open for three years. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30, a fire broke out due to careless work. The raw materials were flammable, causing the fire to spread rapidly. It took about an hour for the fire brigades to extinguish it, but most of it had been burned. Only a small part remains. Fire at Song Park Road 184

The Yin Juchang letter shell workshop at No. 106, Song Park Road, Zhabei, was set up by a certain person named Jia from Danyang. At around 2:30 yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out due to a cigarette butt. The smoke was like a mist, rising through the roof. At that time, the north wind was howling, and the fire was like a prairie fire, spreading to the neighboring house at No. 108. Fortunately, the Zhabei Fire Brigade heard the alarm and quickly drove to the scene and worked hard to put out the fire. It took more than an hour to extinguish the fire. Two bungalows were burned down. The owner of the workshop was ordered by the Public Security Bureau to be escorted by the police for investigation.

Autopsy of a Deceased Chaozhou Maid 185

Seemed to Have Died from a Nervous Illness

A nameless female corpse was found on the side of Xujiahui Road near Beden Road in the French Concession the day before yesterday. After the detective saw it, he reported it to the police station and ordered the detective to go to the scene to inspect. It was learned that the female corpse was about 40 years old, wearing a snuff-colored cotton jacket and blue cloth trousers, rolled up to the ankles. Her hair was scattered and disheveled, and her bare feet seemed to have died of a nervous illness. At that time, because no family members were found, the corpse was carried into the Tongren Fuyuan Hall Mortuary. The detective ordered photos to be taken and instructed the hall to provide a coffin for burial and wait for the family members to claim it. Later, the detective learned that the corpse was a maid in the family of Weng Zhiguang, a Chaozhou native in Tianhui Lane, Bushi Road, French Concession. He immediately notified the deceased's employer, who purchased a coffin yesterday for burial and placed it in a cemetery. According to the employer, the woman's surname was Huang, her name was Yizhen, and she was 40 years old. She was hired in Chaozhou and brought to Shanghai for only a month. Because she suffered from a mental illness, he originally intended to send her back to her hometown on the Taigu Shandong steamer on the evening of the 15th. Who knew that she would go out alone after dinner that night and disappear. He searched for her without success and did not know how she died.

Zhu Guibao's Case of the Brother Seizing the Inheritance to Be Heard Again 186

Zhu Guibao, a woman, previously hired a lawyer to represent her in the French Concession Court Civil Affairs Hall to accuse her brothers Zhu Shengquan, Zhu Jinhua, and Zhu Jinkun of seizing the inheritance and requested that it be divided according to law. The defendants also hired a lawyer to argue that the plaintiff was adopted by her father Zhu Liaotou to others since she was a child and could not file a lawsuit in this case, requesting dismissal. It was instructed to reschedule the hearing. Yesterday, Zhu Guilin, the plaintiff's sister, was also summoned and hired lawyer Lu Shaozong to participate in the lawsuit, requesting an adjournment for further study of the case. The defendant's representative lawyer stated that the plaintiff had discovered that the first plaintiff, Zhu Guibao, had died a few days ago and had lost the right to sue. As for the second plaintiff, Zhu Guilin's request to participate, it is not known whether she is the main participant or a subordinate participant. The court should order the opposite lawyer to answer in detail. Lawyer Lu argued that his lawyer had not yet studied the case and could not express his opinion for the time being. As for whether the first plaintiff has died, it is not yet clear. The judge instructed to postpone the hearing for further verification.

Teenager Committed Suicide Due to Excessive Debt 187

Died After Ineffective Treatment

Wu Chengyu, a local, was only 24 years old and heavily in debt. He had the thought of suicide. The day before yesterday, he went to the Fulai Inn on Wuhu Road alone and falsely claimed to be a guest in Room No. 10, where he secretly took opium. The body was sent to the Pei Lun Road Mortuary. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Xu of the local court of the Special District arrived at the mortuary to conduct an autopsy. It was confirmed that he had died of poisoning. He ordered the deceased's brother, Wu Chengzhang, to sign a guarantee to claim the body for burial.

Meeting of the Executive Committee of the Benevolent Children's Society 190

The Executive Committee of the Chinese Benevolent Children's Relief Association held a regular meeting yesterday in the boardroom of the National Goods Bank. Attendees included Dr. H.H. Kung, Dr. Luo Yunyan, Judge Hu Yigu, Mrs. Guo Bingwen, Mrs. Chuan Bulan, Mr. Gao Fengchi, Mr. Zhang Jinan, Dr. Wu Yicheng, and Mr. Wu Jide. After the chairman announced the opening of the meeting, the honorary director of the association's health department, Dr. Niu Huisheng, reported that in November, the two benevolent children's healthcare clinics treated a total of 1,708 pediatric cases and 61 dental cases. Visiting nurses made 205 home visits to disseminate health knowledge. Subsequently, Director-General Wu reported on his participation in a family work leadership conference in Chaozhou and a visit to the Mind Vocational Girls' School, stating that the family work leadership conference, initiated by the Christian Progressive Association, placed great emphasis on child-rearing, which aligned with the association's goals. The Mind Vocational Girls' School was a pioneering institution in China, training women to competently fulfill the duties of motherhood, a pressing need in society. He expressed the hope that such schools would soon become widespread, bringing great benefits to children in China. Director-General Wu also reported on the performance of two infant nurseries, noting that the mortality rate in one nursery was 90%, while in the other, wet nurses generally breastfed four infants each, with five people, including the nurse, sharing one bed, painting a bleak picture for the future of infant care. Chairman Kung Hsiang-hsi then proposed that the association conduct a detailed investigation and research on infant nurseries in the country, selecting some for practical remedies to observe results. The meeting resolved to launch a large-scale fundraising and membership drive from January 1, 1931. Anyone who supports the benevolent goals of the association could join as a member. All members who joined during this inaugural membership drive would be considered founding members. Donation reward methods would be handled in accordance with national government commendation regulations. It was reported that donation brochures and membership details could be obtained by writing to No. 20, Shanghai Museum Road.

Smuggled Opium Discovered on Inland River Steamer 191

Consignor Passes Blame to Receiving Agent

The smuggling of opium in this port frequently occurs. Yesterday, while the Shenhu-bound steamer "Dali" was departing from Suzhou Creek, a passenger requested to consign a vegetable basket, using a book title, from Shanghai to a village in Huzhou via Jiaze. The Shanghai address was not clearly written. At that time, the crew was busy loading cargo and had no time to attend to the matter. As usual, the freight agent filled out a receipt for the consignor. As soon as the consignor left, the water patrol arrived for inspection and found the vegetable basket suspicious. The water police opened it and discovered a large quantity of opium. The water police deemed it contraband and questioned the crew about consigning it. The crew replied that they were unaware that it was opium when they accepted it. The water police immediately took away the opium. As the original consignor could not be found, they took the freight agent, Mr. Jiang, into custody for questioning.

Shanghai-Woosung Railway Bans Coal Workers from Riding Passenger Cars 193

In order to provide comfort for passengers

Coal workers from the Railway Bureau must travel between Shanghai and Woosung by train, but as there are many coal workers, their clothing is tattered and they are unreasonable, causing discomfort to passengers. The Railway Bureau, for the comfort of passengers, had previously limited coal workers to riding only the work train. However, recently, many coal workers have again been riding passenger cars. Popularity of German Löwenkraft Chicken Extract 195

The German Märkische Pharmaceutical Factory, one of the four major German pharmaceutical factories, produces high-quality products that are universally recognized in the global pharmaceutical industry. Since Löwenkraft Beef Extract was introduced to China, it has benefited hundreds of thousands of people. There is also Löwenkraft Chicken Extract, which is a household staple in Germany. This chicken extract is made using the latest scientific methods from 1970 and contains young female chicken and other tonics. It mainly treats: (for both men and women) general weakness, various losses, five weaknesses and seven injuries, as well as excesses in sexual activity and mental overwork. It is especially effective. One dose of this extract is equivalent to three doses of other chicken extracts. It can also be stored for two weeks after opening without spoilage, distinguishing it from other chicken extracts that can only be preserved for 36 hours. In previous years, shipments to Shanghai have not been sufficient to meet demand. Recently, a large batch of new goods has arrived, and sales are extremely brisk. Local companies such as Sincere, Wing On, Sun Sun, and Hua Lian, as well as various pharmacies and major food stores, all sell it. It can also be used as a gift.

"Staff Annual" Published Yesterday 199

Compiled and Printed by the Staff Union of the Commercial Press Distribution Department

The "Staff Annual," compiled and printed by the Staff Union of the Commercial Press Distribution Department, was published yesterday. Its contents are rich, including calligraphy pieces by Yu Youren, Hu Hanmin, Dai Chuanxian, Cai Yuanpei, and others, as well as many illustrations of artistic works by members of the union. Important articles include "(Our Way Out)," which discusses the current position and mission of the staff union, and touches on the current economic situation in the country. It is divided into sections for detailed exploration and is sincere and thoughtful. "(A Year in Review)" describes the internal situation of the union and the situation of the labor movement. "(The Establishment and Development of This Union)" states that this union was the earliest to awaken in the labor movement and was a pioneer in the Shanghai municipal labor movement. It has had a glorious history amidst hard work. This article provides a systematic record from the time of establishment, which is not only a history of the union but also an important record in the history of the Shanghai labor movement. Special articles such as "(The Process of the Agreed Bonus Distribution Regulations)," "(The Consumer Cooperative Movement)," and "(Deliberations on the Factory Law Draft)" are all valuable texts. Those who study labor issues cannot afford to be without this book. Literary works such as "(Peaceful Smile)," "(Who is the Murderer)," "(Snowy Night)," and "(Hangzhou Dialect)" have sublime artistic conceptions and vivid descriptions. "(The Cycle of Spring)," "(A Connected Book Title Game from Books Published by This Press)," and riddles (related to book titles from the press) are clever, unique, and worth reading. The book has over 300 pages, bound into a thick volume, with a version size similar to that of The Eastern Miscellany published by the press. It sells for one dollar and sixty cents, but there are not many copies, so those who want to buy it must do so as soon as possible (Sales location: Qipan Street Commercial Press, the Union).

The Animal Intestine Industry Trade Association held an executive committee meeting at 2 p.m. on the 21st. Chairman An Jiaxing. Resolutions: (1) Regarding whether to convene a general meeting of members on a regular basis, it was resolved to notify all members to hold a general meeting of members at the Wang Family Residence, Shanghai Animal Intestine Company, at 1 p.m. on December 28 (Sunday). (2) The Binrenji Company and the Zhonghua Company requested to join the association. After checking that they met the regulations, they filled out voluntary applications and paid the membership fees. It was requested to verify their qualifications. It was resolved to separately add them to the membership list. (3) Regarding the case of members Guang Tonghe and Guang Tongchang refusing to pay membership fees, the association sent them registered letters, but they refused to receive them, causing the post office to return the letters. How should this be handled? It was resolved to report the case to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for handling. (4) Since the association was reorganized into a trade association, old members have the certificates of the former Businessmen's Association. However, new members do not have certificates. Should all new members be issued new certificates to unify the management? It was resolved to hand it over to the General Affairs Section for handling. (5) According to the Social Affairs Bureau's document No. 4226, the association's application for registration stated that companies that have not been legally registered must not use the company name. The association does not know whether members Binrenji Company and Zhonghua Company have been registered. Should they be inquired by letter? It was resolved to inquire by letter. (6) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter requesting that the association pay the 65 yuan in membership fees within ten days. How should this be raised? It was resolved to hand it over to the Finance Section for handling. The rest is omitted.

News from Various Labor Unions 201

Huacheng Tobacco Factory Union: Since Mr. Chen Chuxiang, the former manager of the Huacheng Tobacco Factory, took sick leave, it has been heard that he has recovered. The workers of the factory, out of old feelings, have written to the union in various departments requesting representatives to petition the board of directors to urge Mr. Chen to return to the factory as soon as possible. Their feelings are very firm. It is heard that the union has sent a letter to the board of directors stating the reasons for urging Mr. Chen to return and their sincerity.

Xintai Gu Warehouse Union: The union held its 42nd executive committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Chen Quanlin performed the rituals. Matters reported (omitted). Matters discussed: (1) Union member Xue Qingguang of the second branch was dismissed by the management for misconduct and requested assistance from the union. It was resolved that since it is still unknown whether this is the case, Ge Ren and Hu Dachu should be sent to investigate the truth before discussing solutions. (2) The third branch reported that union member Chen Qinchang borrowed salary under a false name and owed 11 months of union fees, which is a complete loss of membership qualifications. It should be reported to the superior organization to expel him from membership, etc., passed. This union was informed by the management that a meeting of all staff would be convened inside the company tomorrow night (i.e., the evening of the 20th) at 8 pm to discuss warehouse business matters. Please be sure to attend on time. Meeting adjourned.

Railway Catering Union: Zhou Weiyang chaired the eighth regular meeting yesterday. Resolutions: (1) The first branch reported that the fifth team reported that the rice and ice distributed by the distribution office often did not match the cargo manifest and requested that methods be taken to stop this. It was resolved to inform the catering section to instruct the distribution office to bring a scale to weigh the goods in the future to show seriousness. (2) Zheng Shengen sent a letter resigning as director of the library. It was resolved to approve and appoint Chuan Meisheng as director and Lang Xinsheng as deputy director. (3) The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau ordered that the National Calendar be followed annually. It was publicly decided to notify everyone and severely punish anyone who is found to be outwardly compliant but inwardly resistant. (4) Regarding the revolutionary anniversary, if members of this union work as usual due to work reasons, the two railway unions should apply to the Railway Bureau to issue double pay. It was resolved to proceed accordingly. (5) The first branch reported that the first team stated that the hot steam tank for storing rice in the carriage often explodes for no reason, and members are not responsible for compensation. It was resolved to inform the catering section to check and record. (6) The first branch reported that the fourth team proposed that when the military police accompanying the train eat in the carriage outside of service hours, they often do not pay according to regulations, causing disputes. How should this be handled? It was resolved to notify the car managers that in the future, military police who eat in the carriage during off-duty hours should pay 20 cents per bowl, while military officers should pay 80% of the regular price per bowl to ensure uniformity and avoid disputes. Meeting adjourned.

Letter to the Editor

To the Editor: After reading yesterday's (December 22nd) report on the establishment of a labor-capital agreement in the pawnshop industry in your "Local News" section, there was a statement that the capital representative Yu Langxi was an outsider and could not attend, and the chairman prevented him from speaking. This is inconsistent with the facts and is based on hearsay, which has caused confusion among my colleagues on the capital side who have been inquiring about it. I am afraid that this will cause misunderstandings and affect the implementation of the agreement. I am writing to request that you correct this information to maintain public friendship. Sincerely, Yu Langxi. December 23rd

To the Editor: I have just read your newspaper's "Local News" section, which reported that the workers of the Zhabei Huashang Public Bus Company were on strike yesterday and mentioned that at 7 a.m., the ticket sellers at the Shishan Road intersection suddenly stopped issuing tickets and put the tickets into the box. The above information is not true and may be a mishearing. After checking, when each car left the factory at 6 a.m. yesterday, all the workers went on strike uniformly. The ticket boxes of the ticket sellers were all automatically placed at the Shishan Road intersection with their money bags and parts. I am only responsible for protection. Also, the name of my position is "schedule worker" and not "ticket seller." Yesterday, in addition to following the union's orders to go on strike, I did not collect or stop issuing any ticket seller's ticket boxes. This matter concerns my credibility, and I am writing to your newspaper to request a correction. Sincerely, Quan Zhongqi.

Automobile News Commentary

Upcoming U.S. Road Builders' Association Annual Meeting 202

The American Road Builders' Association is scheduled to hold its 28th Annual Meeting and Road Exhibition from January 12 to 16, 1931, in St. Louis, Missouri. Attendees at this gathering include road engineers, architects, road administration officials, contractors, machinery manufacturers, and members of the publishing and automotive industries from across the United States. The transportation agencies and organizations in our country have received invitations. It is heard that the China National Road Construction Association has appointed Minister Ding Tiyun to attend nearby. All arrangements for this conference are presided over by experts. The cover design of the order form (see illustration) combines all kinds of instruments, equipment, vehicles, etc. used by engineers and carpenters, which is very eye-catching. The following is a summary of the association's preparations:

Order Form Cover Design

1. Suitable Venue: St. Louis is located in the center of the United States and has extremely convenient land and water transportation. In addition to the United States, representatives from the association's European and American federations will participate. It is estimated that there will be representatives from 34 countries and about 25,000 representatives from the United States. Due to the excellent travel and engineering tours, and the comfort of the hostels, the number of attendees is bound to be greater than the previous session.

2. Exhibition: The exhibition venue is divided into two parts, A and B. The floors are newly paved with concrete and asphalt for easy placement of machinery. Another 7.5 acres of land is used to place heavy and bulky equipment. The open space is 135 meters wide, which is sufficient to accommodate various road construction tools and models. There is also 148,000 square feet of ground for outdoor display. This entire venue is laid out on the ground.

3. Exhibits include various road construction and maintenance machinery and materials, as well as auxiliary items such as automobiles, car bodies, trucks, crushers, road rollers, cranes, drilling machines, excavators, water sprayers, mud dredgers, drainage dredgers, elevators, engines, graders, oil burners, heaters, locomotives, core machines, numbering machines, pavers, joint steamers, planers, reamers, plows, pumps, radiators, road rolling machines, wire mesh, rollers, scrapers, rope, brooms, basket knives, hoes, shovels, bells, saws, scales, rulers, various tools, barriers, markers, snow removal machines, spreaders, spreaders, sprinklers, boxes, dredgers, torches, track, tractors, transportation components, trenches, unloaders, welders, automobile wheels, winches, wire, screws, pliers, etc.

4. The questions for the conference, proposed and announced by Mr. Fan Daoai, President of the American Road Builders' Association, will be researched and answered by various committee members and published in the St. Louis newspapers. The questions are: (1) Road Finance; (2) Road Domain; (3) Roadbed and Pavement Construction; (4) Construction of Inexpensive Roads and Bridges and Their Protection Laws; (5) Road Base and Paving Machines; (6) Transportation Management and Signals; (7) Road Barriers and Appropriate Road Domain.

The most important issues to be discussed at the conference include planning secondary roads, financial management laws, repairing road surfaces, widening road widths, and maintaining urban streets.

Aspirations for the Year 1931 203

New Chevrolet

Price Reduction Attracts Attention from All Sectors

Various Improvements Comparable to Higher-Priced Automobiles

In this year of 1931, with a flood of new car models, a piece of news that might astonish everyone is the actual price drop of the new Chevrolet car. New car releases are an annual event, but Chevrolet's price reduction is bound to pique significant interest in the automotive industry.

The facts are as follows: the Roadster, originally priced at $495, is now only $475; the Sport Roadster has been reduced from $515 to $495; and the Standard Coach has also dropped from $565 to $535. There are three other models with price reductions, which I will not elaborate on one by one. However, the Chevrolet Motor Company was founded in 1911, and the production of roadsters began in 1915. In these fifteen years, its price has never been below $490. This year's new car actually breaks the previous record, which is truly astonishing.

Why did Chevrolet lower its prices? Some people think it must be to cope with competition. However, the truth is far from it. Chevrolet already has a deeply entrenched position in the market. A reduction of twenty or thirty dollars per car will not have as significant an impact as one might imagine. Reliable sources within the company indicate that this price reduction is due to continuous improvements in manufacturing, which have gradually reduced expenses. As costs decrease, the car price naturally follows suit. Chevrolet cars have always aimed to serve the people, and if they can reduce the financial burden on customers even by a small amount, they will strive to achieve it.

On November 8th, Chevrolet held a special public exhibition to showcase the new car. Many new cars have already been produced to meet customer preferences, and they can be purchased immediately. All nineteen branch factories have started production to keep up with demand, as the announcement of the new car will immediately result in a surge of orders, which may be difficult to fulfill in time. Therefore, it is better to start production earlier to be more prepared. The design of the new car is extremely beautiful and has been greatly improved compared to last year. The ride is smoother than before, and the lifespan has also been increased considerably.

One noteworthy improvement is the solution to the excessive heat generated by the engine. In summer, the weather is already hot, and drivers feel even hotter because their bodies are close to the engine. Now, with this new arrangement, it will naturally be much cooler in summer. However, when this heat is needed in winter, it can still be obtained because the heat shield can be installed or removed at any time. The driving mechanism has also been improved, and the brakes are not affected by the weather, so they can be used safely regardless of cold or heat.

The steel wire wheels are beautiful and durable, and the tire size is perfectly matched to the car body. Headlights and taillights are often overlooked, but the new Chevrolet is entirely chrome-plated to prevent rust. Chrome is a recently discovered non-rusting metal, and its value is quite high. The new Chevrolet has reduced its price, but its equipment is comparable to that of high-priced cars, demonstrating a degree of sacrifice. The wheelbase has been widened by two inches, making the interior more comfortable than before, and the seats have also been enlarged. This perfect equipment is naturally welcomed by most customers. Special attention has been paid to safety equipment because the International Road Association's conference resolution on car accidents has notified car manufacturers in various countries to improve their mechanisms, and Chevrolet has paid even more attention to this matter.
